                    Indignation
                    Refine a lot
                        Definition
                            A feeling involving anger mingled with <broken link> or <broken link>
                        Importance
                            Politics
                                Indignation plays a significant role in politics. This is because politicians hold the power to offend many people based the decisions that they make. The decisions that politicians make impact hundreds, thousands, or millions of people. Certain decisions they make may cause many constituents to feel indignant because they feel like those decisions go against what they stand for or believe in, especially if the constituents belong to the same party as the politician. Politicians themselves also feel indignant because if people are not in favor of their policies or are competing against them, they will attack their self-construct. For example, this can be seen when politicians are debating. The other politician typically questions their policies and procedures in hopes to make their competition feel indignant. By doing this, the hope would be that the debate would be stifled.It has been stated that indignation provides the capacity to think through certain situations.[8][9]: 290  The person feeling indignant wants to think about why they are feeling indignant so that they can figure out an appropriate response and pin-point whatever caused them to feel indignant. It has been stated that "when indignation does not express itself immediately as violence, it becomes an investigation of (and what he believes is a more appropriate response to) whatever has caused it"
                        Causes
                            The feeling of indignation can occur when one is mistreated by another or negative feelings are sparked when a situation is out of the normal realm of society. When situations or actions that are considered to be unjust behavior occur, the feeling of indignation is experienced. With unjust actions and behaviors comes to blame. Blame also helps to make up the emotion of indignation. When blameworthy actions take place, the emotion of indignation occurs and negative feelings are projected onto the person who is to blame. Which can be brought on by disturbances that go against social normative. According to Claude Miller, "indignation is defined as a non-primary, discrete, social emotion, specifying disapproval of someone else's blameworthy action, as that action is explicitly viewed to be in violation of the objective order, and implicitly perceived as injurious to the perceiver's self-concept". Indignation is experienced when violations are made to our daily lives. Indignation is an emotion that is considered to be an adaptive behavior. Social environment and social emotions being a stimuli for indignation. Our emotions and behaviors adapt depending on certain situations. Internal and external social norms play a part in experiencing the emotion of indignation. It is expected that everyone coexists and follows the social normative behaviors society has put in place. When something disrupts what is considered to be a social norm, a violation occurs, both internally and externally. A range of feelings are experienced internally, as well as a desire to be removed from the situation externally. When norms are disrupted, offense is taken and the emotion of indignation is ignited.The attribution process is integral in the development of indignation. It is the split-second assessments a person makes (attributions) about their own behavior or in the behavior of others in order to figure out the reason or cause behind it. Behaviors can be classified as situational (external) or dispositional (internal). Fritz Heider wrote that people tend to view behavior in one of two ways; the cause of situational factors or of dispositional factors. From this, an individual is either an Entity theorist or an Incremental theorist when considering event or categorization but is not exclusive to either group. According to one scholar, "People's implicit theories create a framework for processing information, forming inferences, determining attributions, shaping predictions, understanding others' behaviors, and construction representations of social events". Taking this into account and based on a person's classification of entity or incremental theorist (which delineates how a person views behavior in relation to its driving factors), research demonstrates that said person is inclined to experience indignation with more or less frequency and severity respectively.
                        Entity theory
                        Probably move and link here
                            Entity theorists believe that judgements of moral character can be made from merely a few or even a single observation(s). They are most often found making stereotypes about people or events, and believe that disposition based attributions are innate, and rarely ever change. 'You can't teach an old dog new tricks' explains how entity theorists might explain a situation. Behavior, to them, is caused by the unchanging, internal (character) attributes.[5] Hypothetically, if the two different types of people were sitting on a parole board for a jailed criminal, those who exemplify traits of entity theorists might say 'once a criminal always a criminal' and reason that the criminal behavior was driven by the immoral nature of the person and they would do it again, no matter the circumstance, when given the opportunity.Dispositional traits are used within the entity theory as a basic unit of analysis. Either positive or negative attributes are experienced and possibly expressed. With indignation, the attributes experienced are going to be negative. These tendencies are most likely going to remain the same and be predictable with little to no room for change. An assumption is made and judgments are carried out. Entity theory creates and holds judgements based on a single behavioral observation. Once something is believed to be true, it is almost permanently labeled, and objective situational evidence is neglected to be taken into consideration. Disposition-relevant information is the main focus due to the fact that it feeds the reinforcement of negative information.
                        Incremental theory
                            Incremental theorists believe just the opposite position of some entity theorists. They can make judgements of moral character more based on changing external factors (situational) and factors such as effort, desire such as goals.[4]: 18  When formulating judgements, incremental theorists take recent evidence into account and avoid broad character attributions. For example, those of those who are considered to be incremental theorists might argue that, the aforementioned criminal's behavior, was possibly the subsequent result of a poor upbringing or was drug induced, and while, in prison, the incarcerated changed his/her lifestyle through exemplary behavior and service to others. Thus they would not be a threat to the public anymore, in theory.
                        Righteous indignation
                            Righteous indignation is typically a reactive emotion of anger over perceived mistreatment, insult, or malice. It is akin to a sense of injustice. In some Christian doctrines, righteous indignation is considered the only form of anger which is not sinful, e.g., when Jesus drove the money lenders out of the temple in the Gospel of Matthew.[10]The Forerunner Commentary on Psalms 137:2–6 argues that these psalms are about the "bitterness of exile into which God forced Judah", purportedly with the goal of turning grief into zeal, so that the "anger can be used to scour away sin" by becoming "righteously indignant".[11] In John W. Ritenbaugh's comments on Proverbs 15:18 in How to Survive Exile, he argues that it "is alright for us to be righteously indignant as long as we do not sin."[11]Daniel Whitby argues that "anger is not always sinful", in that it is found among non-sinners. For example, Jesus was "angry with the Pharisees for the hardness of their hearts; yet He had no desire to revenge this sin upon them, but had a great compassion for them"
                    Jealousy
                        Definition
                            Desire for the possessions or qualities of another.
                        Envy
                            Definition
                                A feeling of discontent and resentment aroused by and in conjunction with jealousy.
                    Organize this
                        People may not only share emotions with others, but may also experience similar physiological arousal to others if they feel a sense of social connectedness to the other person.
                            A laboratory-based study by Cwir, Car, Walton, and Spencer showed that, when a participant felt a sense of social connectedness to a stranger (research confederate), the participant experienced similar emotional states and physiological responses to that of the stranger while observing the stranger perform a stressful task.
                        To investigate the function of social emotions in economic behaviors, researchers are interested in the differences in brain regions involved when participants are playing with, or think that they are playing with, another person as opposed to a computer. A study with fMRI found that, for participants who tend to cooperate on two-person “trust and reciprocity” games, believing that they are playing with another participant activated the prefrontal cortex, while believing that they are playing with a computer did not.[19] This difference was not seen with players who tend not to cooperate.[19] The authors interpret this difference as theory of minds that cooperators employ to anticipate the opponents' strategies. This is an example of the way social decision making differs from other forms of decision making.
                        in the ultimatum game, two players are asked to divide a certain amount of money, say x. One player, called the proposer, decides ratio by which the money gets divided. The other player, called the responder, decides whether or not to accept this offer. If the responder accepts the offer, say, y amount of money, then the proposer gets x-y amount and the responder gets y. But if the responder refuses to accept the offer, both players get nothing. This game is widely studied in behavioral economics. According to the rational agent model, the most rational way for the proposer to act is to make y as small as possible, and the most rational way for the responder to act is to accept the offer, since little amount of money is better than no money. However, what these experiments tend to find is that the proposers tend to offer 40% of x, and offers below 20% would get rejected by the responders.[23] Using fMRI scans, researchers found that social emotions elicited by the offers may play a role in explaining the result. When offers are unfair as opposed to fair, three regions of the brain are active: the dorsolateral prefrontal cortex (DLPFC), the anterior cingulate cortex (ACC), and the insula. The insula is an area active in registering body discomfort. It is activated when people feel, among other things, social exclusion.[24] The authors interpret activity in the insula as the aversive reaction one feels when faced with unfairness, activity in the DLPFC as processing the future reward from keeping the money, and the ACC is an arbiter that weighs these two conflicting inputs to make a decision. Whether or not the offer gets rejected can be predicted (with a correlation of 0.45) by the level of the responder's insula activity.
                        Research using PET scan has found that, when players punish other players, activity in the nucleus accumbens (part of the striatum), a region known for processing rewards derived from actions[25] gets activated.[26] It shows that we not only feel hurtful when we become victims of unfairness, but we also find it psychologically rewarding to punish the wrongdoer, even at a cost to our own utility.
                        Some social emotions are also referred to as moral emotions because of the fundamental role they play in morality.[10] For example, guilt is the discomfort and regret one feels over one's wrongdoing.[27] It is a social emotion, because it requires the perception that another person is being hurt by this act; and it also has implication in morality, such that the guilty actor, in virtue of feeling distressed and guilty, accepts responsibility for the wrongdoing, which might cause desire to make amends or punish the self.[28]Not all social emotions are moral emotions. Pride, for instance, is a social emotion which involves the perceived admiration of other people, but research on the role it plays in moral behaviors yields problematic results.[10]Empathic responseeditEmpathy is defined by Eisenberg and colleagues as an affective response that stems from the apprehension or comprehension of another's emotional state or condition and is similar to what the other person is feeling or would be expected to feel.[29] Guilt, which is a social emotion with strong moral implication, is also strongly correlated with empathic responsiveness; whereas shame, an emotion with less moral flavor, is negatively correlated with empathic responsiveness, when controlling for guilt.[28]Perceived controllability also plays an important role modulating people's socio-emotional reactions and empathic responses.[30] For example, participants who are asked to evaluate other people's academic performances are more likely to assign punishments when the low performance is interpreted as low-effort, as opposed to low-ability.[31] Stigmas also elicit more empathic response when they are perceived as uncontrollable (i.e., having a biological origin, such as having certain disease), as opposed to controllable (i.e. having a behavioral origin, such as obesity).
                Mood
                    Definition
                        Background, somewhat long term emotions that affect how we react to/feel about things that happen while we have them.
                    Importance
                        Impactful
                            We can react to the same thing very differently based on our mood.
                        Common
                            The vast majority of people experience moods, and their emotions from 
                        Improvable
                            It can be changed chemically to be less harmful, and therapy techniques can change their amount or significance in behavior. Practicing reasoning well even in unideal moods would also make it easier to not fall into acting based on the mood.
                    How moods affect reasoning
                        Even when we become just a little emotional (especially angry/defensive/adrenaline/etc.), our brain places much more emphasis on defending ourselves/attacking the "threat" than we like to think, and this tends to be extremely bad for reasoning.
                            It usually makes it something like 5-25x more difficult to maintain many crucial epistemic habits.
                                Examples of crucial epistemic habits it makes it harder to maintain
                                    Consistently considering ways in which your opponent could be right or at least mean something right (via semantics, implications or logic).
                                    Consistently finding/accounting for nuances in the topic/arguments and thoroughly accounting for how you could be wrong.
                                    Keeping your claims conservative (which tends to cause one to get more defensive which makes the other stuff even more difficult).
                                    Changing your mind when you're shown to be wrong.
                        Examples
                        <broken link>
                    Common factors that affect moods
                        Hunger
                            Hunger tends to put us in a worse mood.
                            Countermeasure
                                Don't make important decisions on an empty stomach.
                        Stressful Events
                            Stress often causes us to be more impatient and get angry easier.
                            Countermeasure
                                Be aware of it, try to reduce it and look at the topic from a broader view if you're very emotionally affected by a small part of it.
                        Hormones and Nutritional Deficincies
                            People often experience getting into different moods than they otherwise would during period or pregnancy.
                            Nutritional deficiencies can affect mood and thinking ability.
                            Countermeasure
                                Recognize when a thought comes from irrational feelings.
                        Mental Health Problems
                            Sometimes they cause or are caused by hormone changes.
                            They can affect mood in incredible amounts.
                            Countermeasure
                                Take it into account and recognize when a thought comes from irrational feelings.
                                Work on it and reduce its effect.

                    Gambling emotional well-being
                        Definition (distinction)
                            The process of taking significant risks regarding one's emotional well-being.
                            Distinction (important)
                                While the negative term "gambling" is purposefully used to encourage being careful, this process is not inherently negative.
                                Infact, oftentimes it is worthwhile, similar to how "gambling" in the stock market (in a responsible way) can be likely worthwhile in some cases.
                                This is not financial advice.
                            Examples
                                A competitive person feeling bad and deciding to play a competitive videogame, in the hopes of winning to feel better.
                                Likely negative example
                                    If they win then they might feel better, but it's likely that if they lose, they would feel much worse.
                                    It might still be worthwhile if the likelihood of winning is extremely high, the well-being reward is very high, the cost of losing is unintuitively low, etc.
                                Asking someone out.
                                    If the person accepts, it could increase well-being a lot short-term, and you could end up with a partner that could greatly increase your well-being.
                                    If the person rejects, it could greatly decrease your well-being, particularly if it comes shortly after/before other negative events.

                Overton Window
                    Definition
                        The range of subjects and arguments politically acceptable to the mainstream population at a given time.
                        Synonym: Window of discourse
                    The window can shift, grow or shrink
                    Acceptable vs true, unacceptable vs false
                        What is more or less acceptable may be more or less likely to be true for various reasons. What is acceptable is never necessarily true, and what is unacceptable is never necessarily false.
                In-groups vs out-groups
                    Definitions
                        **In-group**: A social group to which a person [psychologically identifies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-categorization_theory) as being a member.
                            Examples
                                Religion
                                Political party
                                Nation
                                Family
                                Peer group
                                Community
                                Gender
                                Sexual orientation
                                Sports team
                        **Out-group**: A social group with which an individual does not identify.
                        [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/In-group_and_out-group)
                    Importance
                        Common and impactful
                            People can form [self-preferencing in-groups](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=Om1MkJmG6cRVjw3-V29ukcOK) within a matter of minutes.
                                [Can form arbitrarily](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=x5PmnNWs3WONdr25NvwCwSyh)
                        Impactful
                            [Self-preferencing in-groups](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=Om1MkJmG6cRVjw3-V29ukcOK) can form even on the basis of completely arbitrary and invented discriminatory characteristics.
                                Example: preferences for certain paintings.
                                Example: Sports teams
                            The intensity of "us vs them" thinking exists along a spectrum from mild to complete dehumanization of the "othered" group.
                                Example: pseudospeciation
                            The exact membership of the in-group and out-group are socially contingent (hence vulnerable to the instruments of propaganda).
                        Common
                            There is an innate propensity of the human brain to divide the world into us and them valence categories.

                Information bubbles
                    Definitions
                        A state of intellectual isolation that can result from [personalized searches](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Personalized_search), recommendation systems, and [algorithmic curation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithmic_curation).
                            The search results are based on information about the user, such as their location, past click-behavior, and search history.
                            Consequently, users become separated from information that disagrees with their viewpoints, effectively isolating them in their own cultural or ideological bubbles, resulting in a limited and customized view of the world.
                        [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Filter_bubble)
                        Synonyms
                            Filter bubble
                            Social media bubble
                            Ideological frame
                    Importance / Limitations
                        Impactful
                            There are conflicting reports about whether such activity is beneficial or harmful.
                        Common
                            There are conflicting reports about the extent to which personalized filtering happens.
                    How to recognize when you're in one
                    Related
                        [Ideological frame wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Framing_(social_sciences)#Ideological_frame)
                Limiting environmental influence on reasoning
                    Definition
                        Limiting the extent to which the environment influences our reasoning in ways that it shouldn't.
                    Methods
                        Understanding <broken link> better
                            The more we understand about how we are influenced by our environment, the more we can do to counteract it.

            Sociology
                Definition
                    The scientific study of human society, focusing on social life, social change, and the social causes and consequences of human behavior.
                Vast majority's reasoning abilities
                    [Definition of reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=PN-ghKTcl4UlzOcT7GoE4CIs)
                    Importance
                        Impactful
                            ["Soft" reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=VqyTyvLNbJ6WtfifAe0egZtQ) abilities or lack thereof are very [impactful](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=srdvqoFzlDXmMdtsZoZfaqcg)
                            [General importance of reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=iDTLYnvT3mQLwAaXj65fNdY3)
                        Common
                            <broken link>
                            [Most people frequently have bad goals when reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=QecR8ehYMs7oFAVLyxLw4EwB)
                        Improvable
                            Almost everyone can (if they thoroughly follow this guide) realistically get way better at reasoning.
                                The primary reasons for peoples' irrationality have to do with ignorance of fundamental epistemic ideas and/or bad habits / lack of good habits around applying them.
                                This guide contains the knowledge about fundamental epistemic ideas and teaches how to escape bad habits and learn good ones.
                    The vast majority of people are very bad at ["soft" reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=VqyTyvLNbJ6WtfifAe0egZtQ), including many important types
                        Definition
                            The vast majority of people are very bad at "soft" reasoning, including on many important topics.
                        Examples
                            Definitions
                                Disagree
                                    A vast number of people heavily disagree with __you__.
                                Not primarily ignorance
                                    The vast majority of people would not change their mind about this upon hearing your evidence.
                                        Unless they understood **all** your evidence completely (including like tens of thousands of beliefs in other areas that indirectly contribute), but that would be unrealistic.
                            How to view this
                                The point of this list of examples is to give at least a couple that you agree the vast majority of people are unreasonable about such that the [parent claim](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=7SsiX1YEVBoQ7nJN13LxPAbY) is justified.
                                    As such, the examples don't need to be important, they just need to show common disagreements that are often based on irrationality.
                                You can disagree with the majority of examples and the claim can still be justified if enough people are shown to be unreasonable in the examples you do agree with.
                            Religion / spirituality
                                Disagreement
                                    Number of atheists, agnostics, physicalists, etc.
                                    Number of people who are religious/spiritual.
                                    Number of people who have very different perspectives on religion/spirituality from each other.
                                Not primarily ignorance
                                    Attempts to directly convert/de-convert people to/from a religious positions/denominations based purely on reasoning have a very low success rate.
                                    Techniques which incorporate a kind of emotional manipulation (such as [street epistemology](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=o_wrmnn0YC6kAm7mfGlDdsdR)) are far more effective, indicating that people are often irrational in this area.
                                        Some examples of this and its efficacy can be found on [Anthony Magnabosco's YouTube channel](https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCocP40a_UvRkUAPLD5ezLIQ).
                                        Though keep in mind that he is an atheist physicalist and typically uses SE from that angle.
                                Important
                                    One's religious/spiritual opinions often heavily impact their perspectives on things like the nature/capabilities/dangers of [AI](https://dynalist.io/d/IXRq6OrW0nJs9OGU9TMI5_41#z=AC2FVOtDwykxzJwtFeWeyidz), the correct positions (or lack of correct positions) on [ethics/axiology](https://dynalist.io/d/IXRq6OrW0nJs9OGU9TMI5_41#z=WUj1j0Ov-aaX2CZbDxQXrAKy) and specific ethical issues, [psychological beliefs](https://dynalist.io/d/IXRq6OrW0nJs9OGU9TMI5_41#z=plEkklK0SEl9IlD-DPibunn4) related to ideal parental/educational attitudes (eg. epistemically valuing/rejecting faith due to examples given in holy book(s), or due to a rejection of such holy books), what [political](https://dynalist.io/d/IXRq6OrW0nJs9OGU9TMI5_41#z=snGJLodh9Kcd0Y4K7s8uV0p_) issues are believed to be more/less important and what positions on those political issues are more reasonable, etc.
                            Politics
                                Disagree
                                    Conservatives vs progressives
                                    Economic left vs right
                                    Authoritarianism vs libertarianism
                                    Party disagreements
                                    <broken link>
                                    <broken link>
                                Not primarily ignorance
                                    Attempts to directly change peoples' political opinions based purely on reasoning have a very low success rate.
                            Philosophy
                                Ethics/axiology
                                    Realism vs anti-realism
                                        Important (given consequentialism or similar): Whether or not moral/axiological realism or anti-realism is accurate influences how it is best to try to convince people of one's moral/axiological beliefs. Getting this right is important for most efficiently expanding one's group of believers, which is important for more effectively accomplishing those moral/axiological ends.
                                    Consequentialism vs deontology vs virtue ethics, etc.
                                        Disagree: It's very common for people to believe in deontology and consequentialism to various extents and in various different domains.
                                        Important (given moral/axiological realism): Which broad moral/axiological framework is correct (if one is correct) has a massive bearing on a ton of important goals/decisions in areas such as [abortion](https://dynalist.io/d/IXRq6OrW0nJs9OGU9TMI5_41#z=dXAcb_5RVmG1qtZT674whrLt) and [animal rights](https://dynalist.io/d/IXRq6OrW0nJs9OGU9TMI5_41#z=aTfZw0oQ1jM62EfKQdw6t19m)
                                    Ethical/axiological framework variations.
                                        Disagree: It's very common for people to have disagreements about the particular variation .
                                        Important (given moral/axiological realism): Which broad moral/axiological variation is correct (if one is correct) generally has a massive bearing on a lot of  important goals/decisions in areas such as [abortion](https://dynalist.io/d/IXRq6OrW0nJs9OGU9TMI5_41#z=dXAcb_5RVmG1qtZT674whrLt) and [animal rights](https://dynalist.io/d/IXRq6OrW0nJs9OGU9TMI5_41#z=aTfZw0oQ1jM62EfKQdw6t19m)
                                    Abortion
                                        Disagree: Both pro-life and pro-choice positions have a significant number of supporters.
                                        Important: Depending on one's ethical framework, it can be seen (especially from a deontological perspective) as a kind of crazy mass genocide of completely innocent people which is often considered acceptable and even good. And it can also be viewed (especially from a consequentialist perspective) as a very important feature of freedom/health/happiness, because eg. parents who don't want the child(ren) would likely not treat the child(ren) as well and would likely go through a significant amount of suffering and restriction, and there are eg. situations where the mother will likely not survive the birth and the child may not either.
                                    Animal rights
                                        Disagree: There are a significant amount of people who are eg. vegetarian/vegan for ethical reasons, and a much more significant amount of people who are not.
                                        Important: Depending on one's ethical and psychology perspectives, the mass killing of animals can be viewed as a kind of crazy torturous genocide of innocent creatures. Or it can be viewed as something akin to chopping trees, just the efficient harvesting of resources which has no consciousness/free will/important feelings. Or it can be viewed as something in-between, like treatment that's somewhat too horrible but not of great importance due to eg. some psychological difference between other animals and humans.
                                Free will
                                    Disagree
                                        Number of people who believe/disbelieve in free will.
                                        Number of people who believe in compatibilism vs incompatibilism.
                                        Number of people who believe/disbelieve in genuine randomness.
                                    Important
                                        Punitive vs rehabilitative parenting, prison system, etc., because free will is often considered to create moral responsibility.
                                        Can impact peoples' perspectives on [consciousness](https://dynalist.io/d/IXRq6OrW0nJs9OGU9TMI5_41#z=dckKGIczk90mYQxxh4PIV7Wp)
                                        Can impact peoples' perspectives on [psychology](https://dynalist.io/d/IXRq6OrW0nJs9OGU9TMI5_41#z=plEkklK0SEl9IlD-DPibunn4) - Eg. If we have free will, one could conclude that a substantial amount of our important decision-making cannot be understood, meaning some aspects of psychology, neurology, decision theory, etc. would be much less important than they otherwise would be.
                                Consciousness
                                    Disagree
                                        Number of people who believe that consciousness is entirely emergent vs something fundamental.
                                    Important
                                        Impacts peoples' perspectives on things like:
                                        [Religion/spirituality](https://dynalist.io/d/IXRq6OrW0nJs9OGU9TMI5_41#z=1pCSj98PbE-S3TR4myUGW40g) - Eg. If it seems that consciousness can/cannot be explained within a physicalist framework, one may consider spirituality/religion to be less/more likely.
                                        [AI](https://dynalist.io/d/IXRq6OrW0nJs9OGU9TMI5_41#z=AC2FVOtDwykxzJwtFeWeyidz) - Eg. If consciousness is necessarily non-physical and it would be necessary for AGI, then AGI could be considered impossible.
                                        [Free will](https://dynalist.io/d/IXRq6OrW0nJs9OGU9TMI5_41#z=sXLnfVWldTRqCaP5AG8GRWQJ) - Eg. If consciousness is physical, one could conclude that we likely don't have free will.
                                        [Abortion](https://dynalist.io/d/IXRq6OrW0nJs9OGU9TMI5_41#z=dXAcb_5RVmG1qtZT674whrLt) - Eg. If fetuses (at least prior to some point in development) are not conscious, then it could be considered that abortion is not problematic in that case but would be problematic in other cases.
                                        [Animal rights](https://dynalist.io/d/IXRq6OrW0nJs9OGU9TMI5_41#z=aTfZw0oQ1jM62EfKQdw6t19m) - Eg. If other animals are not considered conscious, we could consider virtually any behavior towards them to be completely fine. If they are conscious, that could cause us to think it's more important to reduce harm to them.
                            Psychology
                                The cognitive abilities of children / the importance of life experience
                                    Important
                                        Placing less or greater weight on life experience than is accurate likely means overestimating or underestimating abilities based on the amount of life experience, leading to inaccurate decisions about how seriously one should treat peoples' opinions based on their life experience, and how people should ideally be educated.
                                        Placing less or greater weight on the feasible abilities/knowledge of children means potentially substantially overestimating or underestimating their abilities, which would likely lead to many important mistakes in many different areas (such as again how seriously to take their opinions and how to ideally educate them).
                                    Disagree - There are a significant amount of people who believe that life experience is extremely important, and a good amount of people who believe otherwise.
                                The efficacy/side effects of punishments and/or rewards
                                    Disagree - There are many people who believe that eg. being even a little soft with kids will cause them to become somewhat spoiled. And there are a decent number of others who believe that it's important to be quite soft with kids. Likewise there is different on whether extrinsic motivation reduces intrinsic motivation or not.
                                    Important - Eg. The extent to which extrinsic motivation lowers  intrinsic motivation has a massive bearing on the ideal design for tons of important institutions and systems. For example it may make more sense to treat children more like animals to be trained much more with rewards and punishments, or it might make sense to use rewards and punishments much less and instead let the children be much more free.
                                Sexes/races/genes having significant differences in cognitive features/abilities
                                    Important - Eg. If the stereotype of females being caretakers and males being providers has a significant foundation in genetics, it may make more sense to organize society more in terms of that. Likewise if that stereotype is largely cultural, it may make more sense to organize society less in terms of that.
                                Ultimate motivation
                                    Disagree - Eg. There are a good number of people who believe and disbelieve in psychological egoism, the position that everyone is ultimately motivated by objectives pertaining to the betterment of one's own situation/feelings/etc. without any intrinsic motivation coming from eg. helping others.
                                    Important - Our ultimate motivation(s) has a significant bearing on what to believe about how to better improve people, prevent corruption, understand how people work, etc.
                                LGBTQ+
                                    Disagree - There are a large number of people who believe/disbelieve that lgbtq+ is (almost) always caused by other psychological issues.
                                    Important - The nature of LGBTQ+ and causes of it has a significant bearing on the ideal course of action/perspective towards it. Eg. If it causes significant issues (like going against what God intended), it may be best to take action to prevent such cases or try to get people to accept their intended state of being. But if it's often the healthier option, it may be best to instead encourage and support it to a significant extent.
                            Misc social issues
                                AI
                                    The consequences of AI content
                                    When will AGI/ASI arrive?
                                        Disagree
                                            Large groups of people have very significant disagreements on how long it will be. Many think it will never come because we are near the limit of feasible reasoning abilities, or that technology cannot replicate free will/consciousness. Many others think that it will be very soon, maybe even in just a few years due to the potential for exponential growth once it becomes intelligent enough to increase its own intelligence by significant margins.
                                        Important
                                            This can have a significant impact on what it makes sense to focus on:
                                            Quicker timelines mean much greater importance for addressing AI safety concerns sooner.
                                            Quicker timelines mean less likely for the bubble to pop and more likely for it to make sense to eg. invest in AI.
                                    How likely is AGI/ASI to lead to doom?
                                        How intrinsically hard is AI alignment?
                                            Disagree - A lot of people believe that the set of goals compatible with eg. Human flourishing is very small compared to the number of goals that would lead the AI to "want" to wipe us out. A lot of others believe that as intelligence increases, things like empathy and moral accuracy will also increase.
                                        Will we get another chance if we build a bad one the first time?
                                            Disagree - People often believe that we will not get another chance if we make a mistake, because we could go extinct or similar.  Many others believe that we would be able to overpower the AI and try again.
                                        What are international race dynamics likely to look like?
                                            When leaders recognize just how powerful AI is likely to become in a short timespan, how much are they going to race vs work together to prevent it from developing too fast?
                                            Disagree - A lot of people believe that a race is likely to emerge in which the world will not be able to properly regulate AI progress, leading to a kind of prisoner's dilemma where everyone develops AI unsafely in order to develop it in a way that is more likely to benefit themselves if they're lucky enough to develop it safely enough. Others believe that we will handle AI in a similar way to how we handled nuclear weapons, which is to say not perfectly but well enough that progress won't go too quickly such that it gets out of control.
                                        What are the chances that an attempt is made to align one or more of the smarter AIs with bad goals?
                                            Disagree - Many people believe that the people who will ultimately decide how these AIs are trained/set up will try to get these AIs to accept goals that most people would consider bad, but which align with their own personal interests. For example maximizing profits, maximizing safety of a country (to the point where annihiliating other countries is a likely outcome), etc. Others believe that this is unrealistic, either because alignment (even with bad goals) would not be plausible, or because of other reasons.
                                        Important
                                            These factors heavily influence how much we as a society should focus on AI safety. Delaying AI development could mean sentencing billions of humans to a significant amount of unnecessary harm, but speeding it up could mean doom and losing the opportunity to try again permanently.
                                Climate change
                                    Disagree - People frequently disagree on the importance of dealing with climate change, and the ideal approach to it.
                                    Importance - If climate change is more significant, we likely want to spend significantly more resources on fighting it. If it is less significant, we likely want to spend less resources on it. If a certain approach is more effective, we likely want policies that are likely to support that approach.
                            ^ Not primarily ignorance
                                It is difficult to provide reasoning for this, but I urge you to find people who disagree on one or multiple of these topics (particularly the more controversial ones), and try to change their minds by giving them the knowledge that you believe they are lacking.
                                If it is primarily a matter of ignorance, you should be able to convince the majority of people you try to convince. If the majority remain unconvinced and can't seem to give good counteraguments (especially if they start giving fallacious counterarguments or repeating points that you already addressed), that should be a good indication to you that it isn't primarily a matter of ignorance, but of cognitive biases and lacking reasoning abilities.

                            [Reasoning short-cuts](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=QbiCWrDMPM38d8BpMPryvG49)

                                [It's common to use the wrong short-cuts](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=zWVET9lI3lrkE-bnS83VGFAo)
                            [We are bad at informal reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=hUZD_olPKQWAyhG7iNc0esm1)

                                [Reasoning vs similar things](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=IaJGr2lc0A403q27gdXVdcVO)
                    The vast majority of people are very bad at reasoning about topics which they have strong convictions about.
                        Conviction
                            Convictions—unlike more typical beliefs—are accompanied by emotional commitment and ego preoccupation.
                        Importance
                            Common
                                Attitudes rooted in moral mandates tend to become convictions. ([Source](https://scholar.google.com/scholar_lookup?journal=Journal%20of%20Personality%20and%20Social%20Psychology&title=Moral%20conviction:%20Another%20contributor%20to%20attitude%20strength%20or%20something%20more?&author=Linda%20J.%20Skitka&author=Christopher%20W.%20Bauman&author=Edward%20G.%20Sargis&volume=88&publication_year=2005&pages=895-917&pmid=15982112&doi=10.1037/0022-3514.88.6.895&#d=gs_qabs&t=1773413447650&u=%23p%3DhDL4X1UwzXQJ))
                                Tedtable vs distal beliefs
                                    In further writings on the idea that some beliefs can become convictions, [Abelson](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9966223/#B1-jintelligence-11-00027) ([1986](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9966223/#B1-jintelligence-11-00027); [Abelson and Prentice 1989](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9966223/#B3-jintelligence-11-00027)) makes the distinction between what he calls testable beliefs and distal beliefs. Testable beliefs are closely tied to the real world and the words we use to describe that world (e.g., roses are red). They can be verified by observations—sometimes easily made personal observations but other times requiring reliance on the expertise of others and the more sophisticated methods of science. In contrast, distal beliefs cannot be directly verified by experience, nor can they be easily confirmed by turning to experts or scientific consensus. For example, you may think that pharmaceutical companies make excessive profits, or that your state should spend more on mental health and less on green initiatives. Certainly, economic statistics and public policy facts might condition distal beliefs such as these (either strengthening or weakening our attachment to them) but they cannot verify our distal beliefs in the same manner that they can verify testable ones. Many distal beliefs embody our values. When they do, they are apt to become convictions, because they will lead to emotional commitment and ego preoccupation, as argued by [Abelson](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9966223/#B2-jintelligence-11-00027) ([1988](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9966223/#B2-jintelligence-11-00027)). Distal beliefs often derive from a person’s general worldview or, in politics, from their ideology.
                                Intuitive example
                                    Imagine you were on another planet (Zircan), otherwise exactly like Earth, and heard from someone that on planet Zircan roses were never red and were always brown. You would have no trouble acquiring that belief. You would feel no urge to argue with anyone that roses can be red. On planet Zircan, they simply are not, and you would have no trouble giving up your belief that roses can be red. On the other hand, if you were to hear that on planet Zircan it was believed that left-handed people were morally inferior to right-handed people, you likely would not accept that belief and in fact would try to argue against it. You would instead defend your belief that the moral worth of human beings does not depend on whether they are left-handed or right-handed. That belief is a conviction for you in a way that the belief that roses can be red is not.
                        The closer beliefs are to convictions, the more poorly calibrated people are—almost always believing that they can provide good arguments for their convictions when in fact they can not. ([Source](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC3735824/))
                        Organize
                        Source
                            This section was essentially entirely taken from https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC9966223/#sec7-jintelligence-11-00027
                Gender/Sex

                        Gender
                        Sex
                    Epistemic gender convergence
                    ~~Expert
                        In general when people become sufficiently reasonable (though it is rare), their habits tend to converge towards an epistemic ideal that involves most of the positive characteristics of all genders and few of the negative characteristics, which tends to make people less like their gender (assuming they have one).

            Self-awareness
                Definition
                    (Amount of) awareness of one's own self.
                Importance / Limitations
                    Common
                        Most people struggle with being epistemically self-aware.
                            We often like to think of ourselves as epistemically immutable in the face of emotional turmoil, but this is often very much not the case even when we feel confident about it.
                                Sometimes because we assume that our reasoning habits/processes aren't substantially influenced by emotions.
                                    Eg. Sometimes it's believed that unless our emotions are really significantly and obviously effecting us, they aren't substantially effecting our reasoning.
                                    <broken link>
                                Sometimes because we're not really aware of our own emotional state most of the time.
                    Impactful
                        With insufficient self-awareness, it becomes significantly harder to realize when we are making mistakes, what kind of mistakes we are making, and subsequently how to improve.
                    Difficult
                        People tend not to be very good at self-awareness.
                        [Bias blind spot](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=qYKn9LjoeqFhKAwabwW925I7)
                How to view it
                    A set of spectrums
                        One can be largely self-aware about emotions but largely not self-aware about reasoning.
                        One can be largely self-aware about some aspects of their reasoning but largely not self-aware about others.
                Strategies for improving self-awareness
                    Removing shame
                        Importance
                            Impactful
                                Shame tends to make us close up/shut down, which makes it much more difficult to engage in useful introspection.
                            Common
                                Defensive/reactionary tendencies are very hard to completely avoid, so pretty much everyone has at least some.
                        Strategies
                    Meta-awareness
                        Definition
                            The [ability to probe]/[act of probing] yourself to become more aware of the things you're doing and why.
                        Importance
                            This allows you to become more conscious of yourself, which is useful for:
                            ^ Better refining your <broken link>
                            ^ Recognizing (and thus having a better chance of counteracting) your <broken link> and how it is affecting your reasoning.
                            ^ Acting more intentionally and overriding automatic behaviors in the moment when it seems best to.
                        Defensiveness
                            https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=GngLFJktj5LSrbeQNe0s1YoN
                        Related   (read)
                            [Introspection](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=aqX299sRiWRL4uS29eOaKCGW)
                                The primary tool to use to improve meta-awareness.
                    Introspection

                        Importance

                            [Epistemic questions](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=W17mij9t81Sv6LWJqdqjiejH)
                            [Emotional questions](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=MjFRIxEgOyepp8XQAUt1d7sO)

                            This includes learning about others, as this can help you get a better grasp of human psychology in general which can help you understand yourself better.

                Different types of self-awareness
                    Importance
                        Impactful
                            It's useful to be able to distinguish between different types of self-awareness.
                                Otherwise it's easy mistakenly assume that self-awareness (or a lack of self-awareness) in some area(s) substantially indicates (a lack of) self-awareness in other(s) when it doesn't.
                                They do different things.
                                    <broken link>
                            It's useful to recognize what different types of self-awareness do.
                        Common
                            Different types of self-awareness exist for everyone.
                    Epistemic self-awareness
                        Definition
                            Self-awareness of one's own epistemic processes.
                        Importance / Limitations
                            Difficult
                                It's easy to be self-aware
                                    One can be self-aware about some of their epistemic processes while not being self-aware about others.
                        Questions to ask
                        Conscious self-awareness
                            Definition
                                Self-awareness about conscious thoughts.
                            Importance
                                Epistemic processes typically involve conscious reasoning.
                            Questions to ask
                                What's a way I could be mistaken that I haven't considered yet?
                                Am I using a fundamentally flawed technique/approach?
                        Related
                            <broken link>
                                Epistemic processes are typically influenced by emotions.
                                Link(s)
                    Emotional self-awareness
                        Definition
                            Self-awareness of one's own emotions and their immediate psychological effects.
                        Importance
                            <broken link>
                        Questions to ask
                            Valuing
                                Why do I emotionally value this?
                            Action
                                Why do I emotionally want to do this?
                            Misc

                Recognizing your redundant arguments
                Might be better under informal reasoning or smth
                    Definition
                        Recognizing when you're making an argument that someone has already addressed.
                    Importance
                        Common
                            It's very commonf or people to make such repeititous arguments.
                        Impactful
                            If you can consistently recognize this, then you can better improve your [habits](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=mwz5Ve2BffIKD_YiMRN4SJOU) for recognizing when other people have addressed your arguments and be more [systematic](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=XUvhNLQybh6UlJJgJCSnbDU7) in your responses.
                            ^ This makes your reasoning more efficient and increases the probability that you will change your mind when it is reasonable to.
                        Difficulty
                            Most people are bad at recognizing this.

                    Critical piggybacking
                    Very likely move to practical techniques
                        Definition
                            Using the criticalness of others to catch the mistakes you make that are primarily caused by your lack of criticalness.
                        Importance
                            Impactful
                                Due to [how](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=hrEJMvz4-YIh1F6g7q3K1fPP) open mindedness is more important than criticalness for critical piggybacking, this typically makes open mindedness more important overall.
                        Requirements
                            Pretty open minded
                                Definition
                                    You must be sufficiently open minded to give the critical thoughts of others enough serious consideration for this process to be very effective. 
                                        Serious consideration
                                        Probably move elsewhere and link here.
                                            Consideration about how the idea could be correct.
                                            Distinction
                                                Not consideration about how the idea "is" incorrect.
                                                    Very important to avoid [confirmatory thought](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=OrIjqF9wWhAuAxUvnk078FOy)
                                Importance
                                    This is much more rare and more important than having <broken link>
                                    Provide reasoning here or link something
                            Decent criticalness
                                You typically need to be decently critical to properly understand the critical thoughts of others and properly piggyback off of them consistently.
                            A sufficiently critical community
                                A community where your ideas will (ideally) be challenged by lots of people with lots of different views, and some people are very consistently able to find whatever problems there might be in your reasoning.
                    Criticalness helps open-mindedness
                        The degree to which one can change their mind when their current beliefs have been challenged is mostly dependent on their ability to consistently understand when their beliefs have been adequately challenged. So becoming more critical can make one more open-minded.

                Evolved reasoning
                    Definition (broad)
                    Importance
                    The human brain evolved to reason badly
                        Evolution is typically a very slow process, often taking millions of years to make significant changes to a species. As such, the human brain evolved for human life hundreds of thousands of years in the past, which is extremely different from the modern life. 
                        The ideal intellectual process is actually not very complex. It really just involves a consistent and efficient application of inductive and deductive reasoning using the axioms* listed before, with decent memory and compute. However for our hunter-gather ancestors, this was not ideal. It requires more energy to calculate deeply with ideal nuance, so evolution supported a route that involves a lot of short-cuts.
                            * [Axioms](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=HTSBFQMP49xI2F7tHDD5P1pd)
                        Evolutionarily-advantageous but epistemically-unideal reasoning short cuts
                            Evolved subconscious/unconscious
                                One such intellectual short-cut mechanism is our subconscious/unconscious (hereafter simply referred to as "subconscious") processes.
                                    <broken link>
                            Evolved overconfidence
                                Evolutionarily, our brain was wired such that confidence is very effective at giving us self-esteem and motivation (good for survival) and seeming capable (good for attracting mates). As such, we are in general somewhat overconfident about most things.
                    <broken link>
                        Inside each one shoudl be an evolutionary explanation.

                    Self-esteem
                    Likely move to emotions and just link here or something.
                        Definition
                            A person's overall emotional evaluation of their own worth.
                        Importance / Limitations
                            Impactful
                                Increases <broken link>
                                    Higher self-esteem can substantially increase our motivation to do things.
                                        Things including learning to reason better.
                                <broken link>
                                    Higher/lower self-esteem implies lower/higher insecurity.
                                Increases <broken link>
                                    Insecurity encourages people to be more fake to be more accepted and protect themselves.
                                Increases <broken link>
                                    Higher emotional estimation of one's own worth tends to lead to more trust in their own judgement, which (on its own) tends to result in a net negative to reasoning abilties due to how great our default overconfidence is.
                            Common
                                Has a substantial effect on virtually everyone.
                                The primary mechanisms underlying this for most people seem to often (or always) be absent from [psychopaths](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=D7Ey-XN074IGrKd4ydeqHorH).

                            Self-hate
                        Evolutionary purpose
                            A nonconscious and preattentative internal gauge (a kind of "sociometer") that continuously measures your relational value (and recent changes to it). Whenever the sociometer needle drops, it triggers an alarm and changes our behavior.
                            Why do people frequently deny this (both to themselves and others)?
                                Because appearing concerned about other people's opinions makes us look weak, and we do a terrifick job of unknowingly tricking ourselves in order to better trick others.
                                Link/create a section on tricking ourselves to better trick others and/or similar concept(s).
                            Source
                                Leary's sociometer theory and experiment on self-proclaimed mavericks (people supposedly unaffected by the opinions of others).

                            People often call credence "confidence". This is the sort of confidence that describes "confidence in" a particular proposition being true or a particular event occurring, rather than propositions/events in general like in [epistemic self-confidence](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=Y9tqRoYVuJ-Fx4nqtdo3klx9).

                    Motivation ≠ ability
                        Definition
                            Motivation doesn't equal or necessarily substantially imply ability.
                        Importance
                            It's possible (and common) for one to be very motivated to do something but completely incapable of doing it (at least in the short-term).
                                This is especially pertinent for reasoning, where people are often very motivated to reason well or perform practices that are very important for reasoning well, but have absolutely no idea how to do them or that they're not doing them well.

                    Common requirements
                        Decision makers learn before forming any opinion that they will be accountable to an audience.
                        The audience's views are unknown.
                        They believe the audience is well informed and interested in accuracy.
                        Why?
                            We evolved to act in ways that can be persuasively justified or excused to others, not to expend so much energy reasoning well unless absolutely necessary. We do this subconsciously, also trying to persuade ourselves.

                Mental stamina
                    Definition
                        The general energy we have for cognitive tasks.
                            Energy: The typical length/intensity we are able to think* for (per session) before getting exhausted.
                                Why "session": We can sometimes "recharge" and return (at least mostly) to normal before the day is over.
                                Getting exhausted: Our cognitive abilities becoming significantly diminished.
                                * Energy can be lost in ways other than thinking, like sleep deprivation.
                        <broken link>
                    How mental stamina effects executive functions
                    Exhaustion
                        Importance
                            Impactful
                                We become significantly exhausted quicker than you might expect during intensive mental activities.
                            Common
                        Recognizing it
                            Signs
                        Taking [breaks](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=T8lQobqEPaFFypMihwloQHLZ)
                    Conserving mental stamina
                        Definition
                            "Conserving" is here used to mean something like "preventing from being lost".
                        Getting overwhelmed
                            Definition (emotional)
                                Feeling emotionally overwhelmed.
                            How getting overwhelmed reduces mental stamina
                                Getting overwhelmed often greatly reduces our mental stamina. This is likely caused by the instinct that dedicating a lot of mental energy to the process is pointless, because we feel like we cannot possibly surmount the obstacle.
                            How to avoid getting overwhelmed
                                1. Recognize when things feel too difficult
                                2.a  Take a [break](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=T8lQobqEPaFFypMihwloQHLZ)
                                2.b  Decomposition
                                    Definition
                                        Breaking a task up into smaller parts.
                                    This allows us to focus on smaller and more managable problems, which tend to feel less overwhelming.
                                2.c  Ask for help
                                2.d  Abandon the task
                                    Typically our emotional instinct is to abandon tasks when they start to feel overwhelming, and typically that instinct is not justified. However just because something is not justified does not mean that we necessarily have good reason to contest it. If it seems most reasonable to abandon the task and you believe you've given sufficient consideration towards doing so and not doing so, then this should certainly be considered a viable option.
                        Taking [breaks](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=T8lQobqEPaFFypMihwloQHLZ)
                            Helpful for conserving mental stamina by:
                            1. Often replenishing some mental stamina.
                            2. Often allowing for a fresh perspective after the break.

                Life experience
                Link to subconscious/intuition and to (importance of) knowledge
                    Importance / Limitations
                        Impactful
                            It's incredibly useful for testing and learning about unknown variables that are hard to account for without experience.
                            Life experience tends not to help much in ["Soft" reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=VqyTyvLNbJ6WtfifAe0egZtQ)
                                Learned and widespread biased and unsystematic thinking tends to prevent us from translating our experience in those areas into useful knowledge.
                                    It tends to prevent us from learning from our mistakes in those areas.
                                    It might be necessary to distinguish between experience and expertise, with expertise meaning “the development of a schematic principle that involves conceptual understanding of the problem,” which in turn enables the decision maker to recognize particular biases. However, using expertise as countermeasure requires more than just being familiar with the situational content or being an expert in a particular domain. It requires that one fully understand the underlying rationale of the respective bias, is able to spot it in the particular setting, and also has the appropriate tools at hand to counteract the bias.
                                        Sebastian Serfas, __Cognitive Biases in the Capital Investment Context: Theoretical Considerations and Empirical Experiments on Violations of Normative Rationality__ (Springer, 2010). 
                                Soft reasoning tends to be about abstract topics which we don't directly experience in a very straightforward or informative way.
                                [People are bad at "soft" reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=qarhXHvwcgUN1n5fnt5sFXck)
                            Most of the biggest things learnable through life experience are typically learnable in other ways.
                                Abstract reasoning.
                                Learning from others.
                Thinking speed
                    Definition
                        How fast one can think, in general or in a particular area.
                    Importance
                        Impactful
                            Higher thinking speed multiplies the amount of thoughts that you can perform in a given amount of time.
                            Higher thinking speed often means a larger amount of thoughts that can be had before short-term memory fades away.
                        Improvable
                            The general idea is to reduce less useful thoughts and increase more useful thoughts.

                Expectations
