            Cooperative reasoning
                Definition
                Importance
                    Helps us [improve our reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=Mcey5J-t6AUuWU92iqr8Nkqe)
                    Expand
                        Cooperative reasoning is very useful for getting [reasoning feedback](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=_raNJnESo8Ou9VQyYZY7wWAQ)
                        Likelihood
                        [It helps us learn](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=4A5HteRemTPGAuXluLQAirau) in general.
                        Likelihood
                    Useful for [learning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=Cf2EDQJtkVrNLpMxmcrhJ6em)
                        **Faster learning:**   There are many very important details in most areas that would require a significantly greater time to learn about on one's own than with the help of other(s).
                        Likelihood
                            **Often lacking info:**   Oftentimes there's a lack of info (or searchability) about the topic in the widely available resources.
                            Likelihood
                            **Often misleading info:**   Oftentimes there's a lot of misleading info about the topic.
                            Likelihood
                                So even in cases where it's easy to find the correct info, it may be hard to figure out which of the info you found is correct.
                                Relevance
                                ^ Thus it may not be very useful to you without spending a lot more time figuring out what info is correct.
                                Relevance
                            Faster learning means that you can learn more.
                            Relevance
                                [Learning importance](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=iotkYGcNyxDt9gMGJJnMhM6_)
                                Relevance
                            [Importance](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=vX_9I-ZrMtjLqyAeXBdlaIA4) of cooperation-requiring knowledge when it comes to you learning from others.
                            Relevance
                        **Human biases** often prevent people from properly learning.
                        Likelihood
                            Humans (at least currently) have [cognitive biases](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=a4amRVifCY8jNCgNpW6j6zB9) that can cause many seemingly quite independent humans to perform the same flawed reasoning.
                                This is especially common when using ["soft" reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=VqyTyvLNbJ6WtfifAe0egZtQ)
                                Relevance
                        **Information exchange limit:**   For a lot of the more complicated and important topics, it is not realistic to share all the most impactful information.
                        Likelihood | Addressed
                            There is too much impactful information to share.
                            Likelihood
                                Due to [emergent simplicity](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=QQDzgaivrRBrqackFuExvxms), it is usually realistic.
                                Likelihood | Arguments will be continued under emergent simplicity's [importance section](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=0p96X6gM6wxgwKdjhfOWrQFN).
                            A lot of the impactful information comes from things like personal experience, which cannot be adequately shared.
                                Generally, there is a low likelihood that one would be lying about their personal experience in a topic like this. So usually personal experiences can be shared to an adequate degree.
                Learning from others
                    Definition (unusual)
                        Learning about things other than how to reason better, from others.
                        Here.
                    Importance
                        [Cooperative reasoning importance](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=ToKUH9kZobFdEN-AU6WWmC3G)
                        Faster learning
                            [General importance](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=Wco2DdiHFrlyRYH-wKF9WZGR) of faster learning from cooperative reasoning.
                    Limitations
                    Find good counterarguments
                        Importance
                            To verify that you're not missing something, you should argue against the best arguments (often given by the strongest advocates).
                                Arguing against weaker advocates usually proves little, because even the strongest idea will attract weak advocates.
                                Arguing against weaker arguments usually proves little, because even the strongest idea will have weak arguments used for it.
                        Find people who disagree
                            Definition (specific)
                                The practice of finding someone who disagrees and learning why they disagree.
                            Importance
                                In order to learn about promising counterarguments/details that you didn't consider before discussing it with them.
                                    This does not require that the people you discuss the subject with are very reasonable.
                                        They could have learned promising knowledge about the subject from other people.
                                            They could be biased towards the other position and accept any reasoning they find, and happen to have found pretty good reasoning.
                                        They could have stumbled across a decent argument by chance.
                                        Confirmation bias tends to cause people to calculate in favor of their own position quite a lot, so if there weren't any subtle counterarguments along the way, they could have a deep line that's good for justifying their position even if they were heavily subject to confirmation bias, close-mindedness, etc.
                                            <broken link>
                            Limitations
                                Oftentimes, the people regarded as the best to consult on the topic will not (at least outside of a paper or book) immediately use many of the best counterarguments or mention many of the important nuances relevant to the topic.
                                Oftentimes the best people to talk to for a given subject will not be available.
                            Finding good disagreers
                                [Measuring criticalness](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=IBGJau5KaVc-QdSibLKAw_4g)
                                Knowledge of the subject
                                Measuring open-mindednese
                                    Open mindedness generally does not matter as much for finding good disagreers.
                            Learning from counterarguments
                                It's important to focus on understanding and adequately representing their position. The point is __not__ to argue with them or prove them wrong, the point is to learn from them.
                                Link goal and strawmanning here
                                Directly
                                    Definition
                                        Learning from them directly, like being in a chat or call with them, or talking with them in-person.
                                    You might also want to ask them to focus on giving you the best arguments that they're aware of, if you suspect that they might otherwise give you worse ones that don't matter as much.
                        Search for counterarguments themselves
                            Definition
                                Search for counterarguments using methods other than looking through the people who make them.
                            Importance
                                [Limitations of finding people who disagree](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=HjwbHT3pi8LNlyk5vnnBJIP7)
                    Facilitate group critical thinking
                        Definition(s?)
                        Importance
                        Questioning others
                        Avoiding openly contesting others
                            Avoid openly contradicting others in situations where the social consequences of openly contesting the common opinion would likely end unideally.
                        Handling people contesting each other
                        Other ways to facilitate objective means of evaluation and critical thinking practices as a group activity.
                        It feels like there should be more.
                Surrounding yourself with reasonable people
                    Definition (specific)
                        Surrounding yourself with people who have the best effect on your reasoning possible.
                    Importance
                        Impactful
                            [Reasoning feedback](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=_raNJnESo8Ou9VQyYZY7wWAQ)
                                Surrounding yourself with reasonable people is likely to increase the average amount of good feedback on how you reason that you get, which would likely help you learn how to reason better.
                                Relevance
                            [You reason like those around you](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=F58Yc-rkCgLlqPQYN9a1f4Dq)
                                So surrounding yourself with more reasonable people will generally make you more reasonable.
                                Relevance
                            [Learning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=Cf2EDQJtkVrNLpMxmcrhJ6em)
                                Being surrounded by reasonable people likely means having easy access to getting their help with reasoning about important things.
                                Relevance
                                ^ This can help you learn the truth about various important topics.
                                Relevance
                                ^ ^ Virtually any disagreement with sufficiently reasonable people (who hold the same relevant axioms) can be resolved.
                                Likelihood | Probably link in eg. importance of reasoning?
                                    [Zipf minimizes required things to consider to resolve a disagreement](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=QJLZsbFm-mktyktapw2vSK7c)
                                    Likelihood
                                    If people agree on the relevant axioms, then they can theoretically exchange all the substantially relevant information required to have all the same knowledge, thus precluding them from realistically disagreeing after that point.
                                    Likelihood
                                    All disagreements about a particular belief must be entirely caused through disagreements about other beliefs.
                                    Likelihood
                                        Distinction
                                            This isn't to say that things like biases don't play a role, just that the way in which they play a role must work through other beliefs. Eg. A bias might make someone hold absurd epistemic beliefs for a time, or manifest __as__ an absurd epistemic belief.
                                        All beliefs can be expressed in terms of [reasoning pyramids](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=dMvgzBqEcT7ia_4DcBqtBeIJ), which is to say that all beliefs are entirely supported by other beliefs, or unsupported by anything ([non-circular axioms](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=HTSBFQMP49xI2F7tHDD5P1pd)).
                                        Axioms are beliefs.
                                        Supposing people hold the same axioms, differences in beliefs can only arise due to making mistakes or having different knowledge.
                                            All mistakes would be resolvable if the one making the mistake had the knowledge that it is a mistake, by getting the relevant knowledge required to come to that conclusion.
                                    Likely resulting in one or both sides changing their mind in a way that more likely corresponds to reality.
                                    Relevance
                                ^ ^ Many disagreements with sufficiently reasonable people (who don't hold the same relevant axioms) can still be discussed in a manner that results in substantial learning.
                                Likelihood
                                    Oftentimes differences in relevant axioms is only part of the reason for the disagreement.
                                    Likelihood
                            [Scrutiny-driven reasonableness](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=L_ujkiY5bfRubhHcMywgm0EV)
                                When one is (or believes they will be) under scrutiny from people they perceive to be well-informed and interested in accuracy, they tend to be more reasonable.
                                Relevance
                                    Perceived **well-informedness** is correlated with perceived reasonableness.
                                    Relevance
                                    Perceived **interest in accuracy** is correlated with perceived reasonableness.
                                    Relevance
                                    Perceived **likelihood of being under scrutiny** is correlated with perceived reasonableness.
                                    Relevance
                                    Related
                                        [Common requirement: audience scrutiny attributes](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=Ac1UXB7JXCOEwWNKKR0jt6_h)
                        Difficult
                            Unintuitive
                                We tend to [believe / feel like] our reasoning is ultimately our resonponsibility, and that we are independent of effects like thsoe that we are surrounded with.
                                    Particularly because there are many cases where we feel we are forced to be surrounded by much less reasonable people, and yet feel they do not have a substantial negative effect on our reasoning abilities.
                                        This feeling is unjustified.
                                        ^ We are almost always very bad at measuring our own reasoning abilities.
                                        Likelihood
                                            [Difficulty of measuring reasonableness](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=WTxRFmcWv9yoBL6ew9GFo7Av)
                                            Likelihood
                    How to do
                        Do not trust your [system 1 thinking](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=Ya-MUAgoHP7_PEgC9ypSAe9I) for deciding who to surround yourself with.
                            [Very unintuitive](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=yUv_lyMWyDMVpOSu7idtaoZc)
                        [Measuring reasonableness](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=GwE6-NAbRo2iIVWkvYqwdzpK)
                    Related
                        Reasonable people would provide a much more reasonable social [anchor/frame](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=gqfxRHs-DUYtXdVA2pFuNEji), [Overton Window](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=uN0SA7RJNS9CHXfwu6uBCV9g), and [in-group](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=BO3hgdXGDMPCMKm_AFmDlaEk).
                        https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=pqLJHM1DMjTBOlRsyi6vQORW
                Isolating yourself from unreasonable people
                    Definition (relatively)
                        Isolating yourself from relatively (compared to how reasonable you want to become) unreasonable people.
                        Isolation from them both in real life and online. Not only standard interactions but also things like eg. watching videos / reading books hosting/made by unreasonable people.
                    Importance / Limitations
                        Impactful
                            Can heavily reduce the influence of unreasonable people on one's reasoning.
                                Would likely greatly reduce [groupthink](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=1krHbDONylAxWz1bingFgOlj).
                                Likelihood
                                Would likely reduce our picking up bad reasoning habits from unreasonable people.
                                Likelihood
                            Likely to lead to (near-)complete social isolation.
                                There likely aren't many people at all who are relatively reasonable.
                                Likelihood | Link to section about lack of reasonable people
                                    Relatively reasonable compared to how reasonable you want to become.
                                (Near-)complete social isolation is likely bad for reasoning.
                                Relevance
                                    Likely to reduce one's [self-awareness](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=02ErcrGfQIBieY8kw6Fke-Nc).
                                        Less opportunity to get feedback from others, to better know of one's own flaws.
                                        Likelihood
                                        [Self-awareness is very important for reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=jAmiCAtQEXf74hKxpluoNgtR)
                                        Relevance
                                        [Self-awareness is already intrinsically difficult to get right](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=LuCflBI3wMIbWnoW2-SD3hc8)
                                        Relevance
                                    If one [surrounds themselves with reasonable people](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=O2iKsShjtUBDRY5QCc-9lI4b) then it wouldn't be detrimental to reasoning.
                                        [It's very difficult to properly measure reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=WTxRFmcWv9yoBL6ew9GFo7Av)
                                        Relevance
                                            Therefore it's likely that in attempting to surround oneself with reasonable people, they would surround themselves with relatively unreasonable people.
                                            Relevance
                                    [Information bubbles may tend to be detrimental to reasoning.](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=kMNpRXMo-vp04h_9eQbkufVk)
                            Can be detrimental to one's social abilities.
                                [Charisma is very important](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=LtcBfo2RuztvWpykt_vhjv1E)
                                If one already has a decent amount of social experience, this should just manifest at becoming temporarily rusty. It shouldn't be too difficult to get back into "social shape" if/when the need arises, so long as there is some warning ahead of time.
                        Difficult
                            To do practically anything, we generally must at least frequently briefly interact with many unreasonable people.
                                This plausibly isn't too much interaction to reap many of the benefits from otherwise isolating from unreasonable people.
                                Relevance
                            Most people become attached to friends/family/a partner/social interaction in general, such that separating would be a very painful process.
                    Related
                        https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=O2iKsShjtUBDRY5QCc-9lI4b
                Common misconceptions
                    [The implications of quick conclusions](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=c14ZK5bPY5TJo_ZbcQAO99St)
                Misc
                    The implications of quick conclusions
                        Very high cognitive speed
                            Definition
                                The idea that when someone comes to a quick conclusion, it is due to very quickly consciously calculating many things.
                            This typically isn't true. Usually the person just had [previous thoughts](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=10Zg_q4wbC_KG0o0ze6nfb2a) to work with.
                        Previous thoughts
                        [Presumptuous reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=HN2qrBZiwD6d8vTcEpYp61yo)
                    Societal counterfactual thinking
                        Definition
                            The idea that on a large scale, we work out the truth via a kind of societal counterfactual thinking, whereby groups/individuals with different beliefs debate until the society is won over by the victors.
                        Importance / Limitation
                            Impactful
                                This kind of counterfactual thinking is quite limited by the general open mindedness of the society.
                                    Sufficient [open-mindedness](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=z7LAOrlY0wVUk3aV25kvfWZe) in a given area is often required to adequately judge the victor of such debates, due to our https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=W7HyxLRMyYcuGQTUpyV2gLDq
                        Related
                            <broken link>

                    [Expression/interpretation](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=K_SHB0cGTZkUKMGU-ep5cX4R)

                    [Reasoning mediums](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=r2dQTPlCik_c_rBtzWzSRO68)
                        Cooperative reasoning is very different depending on the reasoning medium used.
            Common errors
                Heavy [heuristic](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=49rqRClTn-Vx2v-ZXXm90ukK) usage
                Move the "largely based on stupid patterns" kinda stuff into the places dedicated to saying why they're good/bad, rather than being in the definitions, to make it feel less controversial and more understandable. Also perhaps change the name to "topic-specific heuristics" or create a section for that as well.
                    Definitions (and examples)
                        Reasoning that's based on a large collection of heuristics specific to various topics in which the reasoning is applied.
                        Write this (and child) in a better way.
                            Thinking of a subject (or collection of subjects) with intuitive pattern-reaction thinking based on patterns specific to the topic (or collection of topics) for the most part, instead of mostly applying a general reasoning system to all subjects.
                        [Heavy heuristic usage](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=waIk3BhYJ4eBaM4bzQtwem37)
                            People who use different collections of patterns for different kinds of reasoning.
                            They don't super generally [apply concepts or learn things] in [abstract and broadly-applicable] ways.
                        ["Act-based reasoning" here refers to reasoning that's largely based on applying fundamental rules, habits and processes to all subjects.](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=lbqkfxoLw7gwtVVfwrSghuIv)
                        Examples
                            Social rules
                                Family
                                Traditions
                                Relationships
                    Importance
                        Very unreliable
                        Support
                            Almost always heavily contributes to uncriticalness
                            Likelihood | Support | Link criticalness
                            Significantly contributes to [unsystematic reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=XUvhNLQybh6UlJJgJCSnbDU7)
                            Likelihood
                                Unsystematic reasoning [is very important to avoid](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=RD-oTBdlq50cfCjfUvC8a3kJ)
                                Relevance
                        Common
                            Failure to broadly apply good reasoning
                            Likelihood
                                People are often very reasonable in some areas while being very unreasonable in others, in ways that can only be explained by the failure to apply the reasoning typically used in the first area for the second area.
                                Likelihood
                                ^ In other words, a heavy reliance on topic-specific heuristics.
                    How to view it
                        Something to learn to avoid, since it's much easier to learn good act-based reasoning than to refine rule-based reasoning enough to be as good.
                    Forms of rule-based reasoning
                        Causes for different forms
                            Environment
                                Definition
                                    We often learn patterns for rule-based reasoning based on what we feel to be best given our environments.
                                Examples
                                    Conspiracy theorist
                                        In a conspiracy theorist environment, people are much more likely to form positive patterns about claims like the earth being flat, and reasoning common among claims such as that. And negative claims about experts, so-called unquestionable facts, etc.
                                    Good at critical thinking
                                        In an environment that involves good critical thinking, people are much more likely to have positive associations about good critical thinking practices and negative associations with things like fallacious reasoning. 
                        Consequences of the diversity of forms
                            Rule-based reasoning doesn't necessarily preclude good reasoning
                                Rule-based reasoning can in some cases come pretty close to typical act-based reasoning on how well the reasoning is performed for some (or occasionally many) particular topics.
                            Rule-based reasoning can make [intelligent](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=hnV8L0txUJ0M9kO0XbPTh7wP) people very bad at reasoning
                                1. People can learn good patterns for some particular areas but not for others.
                                2. People can learn terrible patterns in general but be highly genetically gifted to be [intelligent](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=hnV8L0txUJ0M9kO0XbPTh7wP).
                    Convincing rule-based reasoners
                        Suggested method
                        Define positive/negative patterns.
                            Definition
                                "good"/"bad" patterns
                                    Patterns that a person has associations with that make them want to agree ("good") or disagree ("bad").
                                    This definition is only meant for this context.
                            Isn't this manipulation?
                                Sort of, but:
                                1. If using a sufficiently broad definition of "manipulation", we must conclude that basically any interaction with anyone/anything is a form of manipulation on such people, because they're usually being irrationally influenced (if influenced at all) by virtually everything due to how flawed rule-based reasoning is. So it isn't as though leaving them alone would make a substantial difference to how much they get manipulated.
                                2. You can manipulate people in ways that benefit them. For example, it should theoretically be possible (albeit most likely quite difficult) to manipulate a rule-based reasoner to become an act-based reasoner.
                            1. Learn the "good"/"bad" patterns
                            2. Minimize "bad" patterns
                                Hide the "bad" patterns until near the end of your reasoning
                                    If you're trying to convince them of a point, usually they've learned "bad" patterns around the common arguments against their position. So if you're going to present one of those arguments (or a form of them), it's usually best to build up most of the reasoning behind your argument in a way that isn't close enough for them to feel like it's the same counterargument they're familiar with. At the end you will usually be forced to use at least some of the "bad" patterns. But you can use the reasoning that they agreed with to minimize the distance you have to take them __after__ revealing the "bad" patterns. Alongside this, you should of course [maximize good patterns](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=HkDeHy_faRaPRhBO64fnrXlC)
                                Words/phrases
                                    Words/phrases are a very common source of "good"/"bad" patterns.
                            3. Maximize "good" patterns
                                [Characterization](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=-RfRZ7650bJF8cl3dEY8_zE_)
                                [Words/phrases](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=MGVb7u212ZC-hOMhZTWtA-AO)
                    Act-based reasoning
                        Definition
                            "Act-based reasoning" here refers to reasoning that's largely based on applying fundamental rules, habits and processes to all subjects.
                                Distinction
                                    This still involves learning patterns and doesn't mean the absence of sbuconscious/intuition or the learning/application of irrational patterns for certain subjects.
                        Limitations
                            Act-based reasoning can still be irrational if the fundamental rules being applied to all subjects are flawed.
                                The set of fundamental rules doesn't necessarily have to be the same as the set of axioms that the person accepts.
                        Indications of act-based reasoning
                        ~Expert
                            Asks why a lot maybe? Debates when disagrees even as a child? Maybe caused by parents entertaining questions?
                        [Systematic reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=XUvhNLQybh6UlJJgJCSnbDU7)
                Confirmatory thought
                    Definition
                        A reasoning process focused on justifying a pre-existing belief, where the mind selectively searches for, interprets, and remembers information that supports what it already thinks is true.
                        Distinction
                            In some cases it can appear quite similar to someone who isn't doing this kind of reasoning, but who's focused on representing their position with all the arguments they think of first, and who doesn't acknowledge when they agree or think of counterarguments against their arguments.
                    Importance / Limitations
                        Common
                            [Confirmation bias](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=_Dn0UzSi_JF-Rno7Uvb0luL-) is [common](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=-ydpOA4gbPjdmKKxg8w6xD8p).
                        [Importance/limitations of starting with conclusion](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=Cu3RSaK4pPHrIt7Nykla2fjb)
                        [Importance/limitations of assuming that you're right](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=8ojZB8gOuk6R2ugB4oFivsU4)
                        [Importance/limitations of assuming that others are wrong](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=Rp5c1SqHvNU_BDsfyKqpro2X)
                        [Importance/limitations of reasoning to convince others](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=Z8wUBsj-8iBgQFuqtj3eI2xU)
                    1. Starting with conclusion
                        Definition
                            Typically
                                In large part directed by [system 1 thinking](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=Ya-MUAgoHP7_PEgC9ypSAe9I)
                                Involving a strong feeling that the conclusion is true.
                        Importance / Limitations
                            Common
                                [Confirmation bias](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=_Dn0UzSi_JF-Rno7Uvb0luL-) contributes to how common it is.
                                The way that [system 1 thinking](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=Ya-MUAgoHP7_PEgC9ypSAe9I) works contributes to how common it is.
                                You will find plenty of mention of how common it is in the relevant literature.
                            Impactful
                                High propensity for bad thinking
                                    [Confirmation bias](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=_Dn0UzSi_JF-Rno7Uvb0luL-)
                                    Likelihood
                                    [Heavy heuristic usage](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=waIk3BhYJ4eBaM4bzQtwem37)
                                    Likelihood
                                        Because this often feels like stronger evidence than it is, and when under the influence of confirmation bias, one will accept this evidence without thinking further to consider the possible counters.
                                    [Cherry-picking](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=VCYeE_G2-lkwQ6_S-w6A9idu)
                                    Likelihood
                                    **Often causes:**   [assuming that you're right](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=oWcWJUZA0MYOjqvk9I0l2G7E)
                                    Relevance
                                Can sometimes be temporarily helpful
                                    Eg. When considering hypotheticals
                                    Link hypotheticals
                                        Eg. When [Steelmanning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=LWB8YQUQupE7UQRtFL7J9g6w)
                        Often causes
                            [Assuming that you're right](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=oWcWJUZA0MYOjqvk9I0l2G7E)
                            Evolutionary social instincts to defend opinion
                            Expand and link, maybe link to the open mindedness section about emotions or smth
                    2. Assuming that we're right
                        Definition (specific)
                            Concluding that we're right with inadequate justification.
                        Importance / Limitations
                            Common
                            Impactful
                            ^ Often causes [assuming that other(s) are wrong](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=525oYS_TiO4rZW4aUGvWXESU).
                        Causes
                            Typically caused by [starting with the conclusion](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=PIiCWPph1BqajBwPGPDQGbWC)
                    3. Assuming that other(s) are wrong
                        Definition (specific)
                            Believing that the other person of wrong without adequate justification.
                        Importance / Limitations
                            Common
                            Limitations
                            ^ Often causes [assuming the worst](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=-jUllZ4uoC33mBPDTPjLyI3l)
                        Assuming the worst
                            Definition
                                Overconfidently believing that other(s) are stupid or have bad intentions rather than having different knowledge that leads to a different result, or believing otherwise due to a mere minor error.
                            Causes
                                [Assuming that other(s) are wrong](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=525oYS_TiO4rZW4aUGvWXESU)
                        Causes
                            Typically largely caused by [assuming that you're right](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=oWcWJUZA0MYOjqvk9I0l2G7E)
                            Often partially caused by [lacking context](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=lVuocPQtbJr1T1UQTA9_LCyy)
                    4. Reasoning to convince others
                        Definition
                            Reasoning primarily to convince others, rather than to find the truth.
                        Importance / Limitations
                            Common
                            Impactful
                            ^ [Importance / Limitations of "winning"](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=bHYsU7G2hrBNIUdF9-dmDjsv)
                        Causes
                            [Assuming that you're right](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=oWcWJUZA0MYOjqvk9I0l2G7E)
                            [Assuming that other(s) are wrong](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=525oYS_TiO4rZW4aUGvWXESU)
                    Common causes/excuses
                        [Confirmation bias](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=_Dn0UzSi_JF-Rno7Uvb0luL-)

                    Related
                        [Confirmation bias](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=_Dn0UzSi_JF-Rno7Uvb0luL-)
                        [Rationalization](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=NaE-8bpB1ZDuRzcl_T3nNErK)
                            The most common form of confirmatory thought, involving beginning with a conclusion that was derived from [system 1 thinking](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=Ya-MUAgoHP7_PEgC9ypSAe9I).
                        [Cherry picking](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=VCYeE_G2-lkwQ6_S-w6A9idu)
