                    Immediate correctness
                        Definition
                            Being correct about the immediate thing.
                        Importance
                            Impactful
                                Immediate correctness doesn't matter as much as correctness in general.
                                    Correctness in general is dependent on overall reasoning performance rather than immediate correctness.
                                        The way to improve overall reasoning performance is by looking at how you reason in the short-term.
                                [Correctness ≠ good reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=7CPFMBYoWL3Y9vzhHpyxUynq)
                            Common
                                [People tend to think being correct entails that they used good reasoning to get there](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=ivsAcg-6ZeX4rW9rr47C2YFf)
                                Immediate correctness is usually less important than the reasoning used to get there.
                                    The reasoning used to get there: How well you reasoned to arrive at your conclusion.
                        Correctness ≠ good reasoning
                            Importance
                                Impactful
                                Common
                                    [People tend to think being correct entails that they used good reasoning to get there](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=ivsAcg-6ZeX4rW9rr47C2YFf)
                            People tend to think being correct entails that they used good reasoning to get there.
                                People give themselves feedback in accordance with how close/far they believe they are from the truth, rather than how well they reasoned.
                                    This usually leads them to do behaviors that make them feel closer to the truth, which often don't actually get them closer to the truth.
                                    Types
                                        Reason well but still far from truth
                                            Definition
                                                We sometimes go "ah, I was wrong" and think of it as a mistake, when really it was just bad luck or lacking important evidence.
                                            Limitations
                                                This is much less common than [reasoning badly but still close to the truth](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=HW8-uQkaHQKIem3_7Y7ti_K8) because we tend to be biased towards <broken link>, at least intellectually.
                                        Reason badly but still close to truth
                                            We often go "ah, so I was right!" and focus on that, regardless of whether we reasoned well to get there.
                        <broken link>
                    "Winning"
                        Definition (broad)
                        Importance / Limitations
                            Common
                                People often focus on "beating the opponent", "winning the debate", etc.
                            Impactful
                                **Prioritizes bad reasoning and deprioritizes good reasoning:**   "Winning" debates is typically measured in terms of metrics that significantly differ from good reasoning. So focusing on "winning" typically entails deprioritizing good reasoning to some extent, and prioritizing those other metrics.
                                    How convinced the audience is
                                        [Persuasion strategies that don't prioritize reasoning tend to convince people more](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=0WKmMK8w3_icwUoGQAzc3vT9)
                                            Most debates involve a lot of ["soft" reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=VqyTyvLNbJ6WtfifAe0egZtQ)
                                                Therefore people are much more likely to be irrational about them.
                                                Relevance | Link to a section about how people tend to be more irrational about soft reasoning, once it's available.
                                            Therefore we're encouraged to use such strategies, especially subconsciously from past experiences of them working better.
                                            We're often taught to use these strategies in thinks like debate classes.
                                            Eg. [Characterization](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=-RfRZ7650bJF8cl3dEY8_zE_)
                                    How stumped the opponent is
                                        Stumping the opponent is much easier with rhetoric and fallacies than with good reasoning/solid sources.
                                        This has to do with how unreasonable opponents and the audience tend to be.
                                [Encourages confirmatory thought](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=OrIjqF9wWhAuAxUvnk078FOy)
                                    "Winning" in this context means successfully defending a certain conclusion, so the natural instinct is to start with that conclusion in one's thinking and try to justify/defend it.
                        Related (many very related sections)
                            [Persuasion](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=S-S1oq4cZbPSPeH4eYJKd9K7)
                                Limitations
                                    Not a good indication of truth
                                        Most people (probably even among groups who you would expect to be exceptions) are pretty uncritical, so convincing them is not a good indication of your point being correct.
                            [Competition](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=436tjnAmv5CrbzS3opf2Vin_)
                            [Refutation](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=vGnU05OJtfhN092NcMo2TQ36)
                            [Correctness ≠ good reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=7CPFMBYoWL3Y9vzhHpyxUynq)
                    Refutation
                        Definition
                            Prioritizing refuting others' points.
                        Importance
                            Impactful
                            Common
                                Often we get into a mindset of prioritizing finding what's wrong with opposing arguments and counterarguments.
                                    This isn't necessarily a bad thing.
                        How to view it
                        Depends on rank.
                            A mindset to largely avoid for now.
                            ≤ ~Adept
                            A useful tool that should usually be used when there are important ideas that aren't being questioned much.
                            ≥ ~Advanced
                        Pros / Cons
                            Prioritizing refutation tends to reduce the amount of effort we put into understanding and being open to opposing ideas.
                                It is crucial for good reasoning to often heavily prioritize <broken link> such claims.
                            Can help a lot with finding hard-to-find flaws or counterarguments.
                            ~Advanced
                        <broken link>
                Goals of discussions
                Maybe combine with goals of reasoning or something?
                    Importance
                        Impactful
                            Goalless discussion
                                Discussion without a goal often doesn't provide much benefit.

            Memory
                Importance
                    Common
                    Improvable
                        Currently bad
                            The vast majority of people aren't very good at memory
                            Likelihood
                            People are typically substantially overconfident about memory.
                            Likelihood
                                They're typically much more forgetful than they assume themselves to be.
                Keeping track of context
                    Definition
                        Keeping track of what arguments support what other arguments.
                    Importance
                        Common
                            It's very common for people to keep track of the context at least a bit.
                        Impactful
                            Useful for seeing if argument(s) (whether your own or someone(s) else's) provide sufficient weight (whether for or against) to their target.
                                Helpful for [reasoning self improvement](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=Mcey5J-t6AUuWU92iqr8Nkqe)
                                Relevance
                        Improvable
                            It's rare for people to systematically keep track of the context, and thus very common for people to fail to keep track of it in major ways.
                    Techniques
                        [[Mostly-normal text](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=YqxhIh8cQC3UlXflwRLyqM1B)]-specific
                            Definition
                                Techniques that are largely only useful for mostly-normal text.
                            Importance
                                [Importance of mostly-normal text](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=ztxLHqTD5SAcfKIwE5GTmXz9)
                            Frequently checking message history
                                Definition
                                    Frequently checking previous messages to better understand how the arguments fit together.
                                Importance / Limitations
                                    Impactful
                                        Very important for [thoroughness](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=lj9jejrk2s5bCXgZLKLHwWkZ) in mostly-normal text discussions.
                                            [Importance of thoroughness](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=v06MMtLk-l69FN8yrpApO2BV)
                                            Relevance
                                        Takes a lot of extra time
                                            Can often be done while waiting for other person(s)'s response(s).
                                            Relevance
                                Related
                                    [Habits](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=rbfReKt_odNwwwIDWESiYqq-)
                                    ^ Realistically this would likely have to be a habit to be performed consistently enough to be substantially helpful.
                            Linking relevant messages
                                Definitions
                                    Adding links in your text responses, that allow you and the person(s) you're messaging with to quickly find relevant past message(s).
                                    **Message history:**   By message history, we just mean the messages that were sent a bit more than slightly previously.
                                        Maybe messages sent at least [500 characters] or [1 hour] ago.
                                Importance / Limitations
                                    Impactful
                                        Often useful for immediately clearly showing context.
                                            Useful for resolving situations where other person(s) aren't properly keeping track of the context.
                                            Relevance
                                                It allows the other person to look back at their own message(s).
                                                Likelihood
                                                [Cost of misunderstandings](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=1qtW0Q9lO1KZeMzP6UFlafQo)
                                                Relevance
                                            Takes time to find messages to link.
                                            Relevance
                                                It takes barely any extra time if you're already [frequently checking message history](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=HvFzVSKgZMdfLOLgOwq2DPux)
                                                Relevance
                                        Often useful to later you.
                                            Eg. For finding a particular message/quote.
                                            Likelihood
                                            ^ Allows you to double-check context that's relatively important to get right.
                                            Relevance
                                                Eg. Another person's message.
                                                Relevance
                                                ^ [Cost of misunderstandings](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=1qtW0Q9lO1KZeMzP6UFlafQo)
                                                Relevance
                                        Getting into the habit of doing this implicitly helps get into the habit of [frequently checking message history](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=HvFzVSKgZMdfLOLgOwq2DPux).
                                            [Habits](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=rbfReKt_odNwwwIDWESiYqq-)
                                            Likelihood
                                            You often have to check the message history in order to find the one you're wanting to link.
                                            Likelihood
                                        Not always possible.
                                            Depending on the platform, it may not allow you to link to a particular message.
                                            Likelihood
                                            Most platforms allow for message linking in some form.
                                            Relevance
                                                **Reply-link only:**   If you're restricted to only being able to link to messages you're replying to, you can send several messages that each reply to particular messages you're wanting to link to.
                                                Likelihood
                                                    It works
                                                    Relevance
                                                    It's awkward
                                                    Relevance
                            Quoting relevant messages
                                Definition (important distinction)
                                    Adding a quote of previous text in your text responses.
                                    Distinction (important)
                                        This doesn't necessarily mean making a quote in text separate from the reply preview.
                                        Depending on the platform and the length of the message being replied to, sometimes the little preview thing showing the message that's being replied to is sufficient to act as a quote, and that would count as "quoting relevant message" here.
                                Importance / Limitations
                                    Impactful
                                        [Importance of linking relevant messages](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=kwz4a6-vQlUvJS8gQtGZuTXH)
                                        ^ Has virtually the same importance arguments as this section would have, except of course for saying things like "link"/"message" instead of things like "quote".
                    Related (very)
                        [Lacking context](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=lVuocPQtbJr1T1UQTA9_LCyy) (very related)
                            A big part of keeping track of the context is effectively resolving situations where you're lacking some context.
                Chunking
                Look into this and likely move it into one or multiple of the categories.
                    Definition
                        [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chunking_(psychology))
                Evolutionary explanation for memorability
                    We evolved to pay special attention and carefully memorize things like stories, people, landmarks, visual features in general, etc.
                    We did not at all evolve to memorize it focus on abstract concepts or values like numbers, words or anything like that.
                    This is why encoding abstract things we didn't evolve to memorize into things we did evolve to memorize can be so effective.
                Compression
                    Memorizing results
                        Definition
                            While trying to find an ultimate answer to a complicated question involving many smaller parts, after solving each smaller problem, focus on remembering only the result of that part.
                            Examples
                                Remember only whether a conclusion is true or false, and then move on to the next small question.
                                Remember only the cost and value of the object you are comparing to others, then move on to evaluating the next object.
                    Single word technique
                    Not an official name.
                        Definition
                            The memory technique where each item in a list of things (typically tasks) is boiled down to one word.
                Increasing memorability
                    Notable specificity
                        Definition
                            The technique of imagining a specific instance of something with very memorable features.
                            Example
                                Hairbrush
                                    Think of a specific hairbrush you use or something.
                                    Imagine fiery flames on the handle.
                                    Imagine the bristles as hair.
                        Absurdity
                            Typically the more absurd something is, the more memorable it is, even if it's fictitious. So adding absurd, fictitious specificity in your head can help a lot with memorability.
                        [Practice](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=7uTPFcFISeOZWgi6CC8b3Q50)
                            This improves memory in general, because it becomes easier to encode things with specific, memorable details.
                    Add relations
                        Definition
                        Relations between memory items
                            Definition
                                Adding relations between multiple things that you want to memorize.
                                Example
                                    Combining a hairbrush, soy sauce, socks, giraffe and biplane by imagining the girafe bathing in a bathtub of soy sauce brushing its hair with the hairbrush, all on top of a biplane.
                            Memory palace
                                Definition
                                Categories
                                    If there's a risk of you getting categories confused with each other, imagine some kind of entrance/container for knowledge in those categories and add distinctive details to that entrance/container so the categories are memorable from each other.
                                    Ideally it should feel natural and obvious to you.
                                Refinement
                                    Definition
                                        Spending time "walking around" your memory palace to solidify it and refine relations, to prevent forgetting important details and practice using it to make it more easy to deal with in the future.
                                Example
                                    Rooms
                                        Definition
                                            Imagining a room for each topics you want to store memories about.
                                        Doors
                                            Give each room a distinct door so that they don't blend together.
                                        Containers
                                            Definition
                                                Example
                                                    Drawers
                                        Memory items
                                            Examples
                                                A tiny river with a beaver dam to memorize the process a beaver uses to build the dam.
                        <broken link>
                            Specific and memorable relations are especially effective.
                        [Practice](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=7uTPFcFISeOZWgi6CC8b3Q50)
                            This improves memory in general, by making it easier to form creative relations between things.
                    Repetition
                    Oral statement
                    Sources
                        A lot of information about this was pulled from this video: ["The simple memory trick that changed my life"](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=w8JuHaRQmUs)

                        Definition
                            Use an encoding system to encode numbers into other concepts.

                                Especially in cases where you would likely otherwise be subject to over-reliance on [system 1 thinking](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=Ya-MUAgoHP7_PEgC9ypSAe9I)

                                Relevance
            Consistency in reasoning
                Definition
                Improve
                    How consistent one can reason.
                Importance
                    Becomes especially important in the context of [reasoning pyramids](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=dMvgzBqEcT7ia_4DcBqtBeIJ)
                        Consistency or inconsistency can result in radically different chances of successfully computing a reasoning pyramid, due to the compounding chances.
                    [It's usually easy to blunder in reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=vVak2mVU77754LQY5rltVT1_)
                Blunders
                    Definition
                    Importance
                        It's usually easy to blunder in reasoning
                            [The instability of large reasoning pyramids](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=wF3wChw5a-nl2FeRaQTbTP7Q)
                            Analogies
                                Chess is like reasoning, and it's easy to blunder in chess.
                        It's often very consequential
                        Should include more or something
                            [Reasoning blunders in crucial areas are common](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=0SbisTdpRtnWks8DNCqswDYR)
                        Feedback is not guaranteed
                            It's quite possible (and common) for people to use reasoning built on a blunder for important decisions all throughout their entire life without ever realizing it.
                                Examples
                                    Religious people
                            So it is incredibly important to do many thorough and varied checks for blunders in your own reasoning.
                    Avoiding blunders
                        Checking past reasoning
                            What beliefs to check
                                The fundamental beliefs that underly many important beliefs.
                                The beliefs that there is not clear feedback for being right/wrong.
                                The beliefs that require a lot of ["soft" reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=VqyTyvLNbJ6WtfifAe0egZtQ) to arrive at.
                                    Why?
                                        These kinds of beliefs tend to be where we make the most errors, because we cannot use solid reasoning (eg. math) for them.
                                    Examples
                                        Religion/spirituality
                                        Politics
                                        Most philosophy
                                        Some psychology
                            How to check
                Related
                    [Systematic reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=XUvhNLQybh6UlJJgJCSnbDU7)
                        An extremely useful practice for increasing consistency.
                    [Multiple checks](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=xY0Z4_L3g_saqIIVdvA81Uuh)
                        A very useful technique for increasing consistency.
            Measuring reasonableness
                Importance / limitations
                    Impactful
                        **Measuring own reasoning:**   Being able to accurately measure reasoning likely means being able to measure your own reasoning.
                            Measuring your own reasoning likely means being less overconfident, undercontident, and ignorant about what helps/harms your reasoning.
                            ???
                            Measuring one's own reasoning accurately is very difficult.
                            Relevance
                        **Learning limitations:**   Learning about the limitations of method commonly used to measure reasoning will allow you to avoid relying on those methods, allowing you to avoid drastic mistakes involving overestimating your own reasoning or underestimating others' reasoning (or vise versa).
                    Difficult
                        Most of the common methods are very unreliable.
                        Move?
                        It is very difficult to do reliably.
                Measuring [epistemic humility](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=gh0FW_-AcyLbpnuFvEWm45Ke)
                Measuring [criticalness](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=CDQTVmFBdUrFvIU4T3JfvdWZ)
                Measuring reasonableness in general
                    IQ
                        Definition
                            Intellectual quotient
                        Importance / limitations
                            Common
                                IQ is very commonly used as a measurement of reasoning.
                            Impactful
                                IQ is not very highly correlated with reasoning.
                                    IQ does not appear to have mechanisms for measuring [soft reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=VqyTyvLNbJ6WtfifAe0egZtQ) biases.
                                    Likelihood
                                        Soft reasoning biases have a significant impact on our general ability to change our mind when our current beliefs are adequately challenged.
                                            Thus they have a significant impact on our [intellectual humility](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=gh0FW_-AcyLbpnuFvEWm45Ke), thus they have a significant impact on our reasoning abilities.
            Misc
                [Enthymemes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enthymeme)
                    **Definition:**   Arguments with hidden premise(s).
                        Hidden premises:
                        ^ Unstated propositions that are required for an argument to be valid and/or sound.
                            The unstated propositions can be ordinary premises, or inference rules (because an inference rule can be thought of as a type of premise).
                            Explain why in the section for inference rules, which will likely be in [Axioms](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=HTSBFQMP49xI2F7tHDD5P1pd), and then link that explanation here.
                        ^ **Synonym:**  Unstated assumptions
                        Example
                            "**Socrates is mortal because he's human**."
                            ^ The complete formal syllogism
                            Relevance
                                All humans are mortal. (major premise – unstated)
                                Socrates is human. (minor premise – stated)
                                Therefore, Socrates is mortal. (conclusion – stated)
                    Importance
                        Common
                General software considerations
                    Centralization
                        Definition
                            The software (and/or the server(s) for it) being centralized.
                        Importance
                            Your data is potentially at risk since the servers could shut down at any time, especially if they're meant for a small site/service that doesn't make much money.

        Expression/interpretation
            Importance
                Impactful
                ^ Reduce misunderstandings
                Both your own and others'
                    **Relevance of the interpretation/expression section:**   Misunderstandings are caused by lacking expression/interpretation abilities. This section is about expression and interpretation.
                    Relevance
                    Cost of misunderstandings
                        **Exponential misunderstandings:**   While trying to resolve a misunderstanding, more misunderstanding(s) can arise, at a rate faster than they are resolved.
                        Relevance
                            When this happens, it's easy for the amount of required work to resolve the original misunderstanding to grow exponentially until a massive amount of terms have had to be defined, a massive amount of ideas have had to be clarified, etc.
                            Relevance
                                Where there is one misunderstanding, there is often ample room for many more.
                                Likelihood
                            Learning interpretation/expression can greatly reduce the rate of misunderstandings arising, and the speed at which you can resolve them.
                            Relevance
                        Cost of unresolved misunderstandings (high)
                            Often, some misunderstandings are crucial to resolve in order to  efficiently continue with the reasoning interaction where the misunderstandings arose.
                                Knowledge piggybacking
                                Create and link
                                    https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=ab0k5w-abYxOLCZM9aOYOhgR
                                [Critical piggybacking](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=2J5emCtKut8DRA6avr2C4r87)
                                    In order to consistently and effectively perform this piggybacking, you cannot back out of discussions where misunderstandings arise.
                                        Often even if there are lots of them, and lots are primarily caused by other party(s).
                                        Relevance
                                        Because most people are not very good at interpretation/expression, even people who have great counterarguments that you haven't heard before.
                                        Likelihood
                                            So it's important to learn to be the primary driver of resolving misunderstandings.
                                            Relevance
            Interpretation
                Importance
                    Common
                        Interpretation underlies virtually all communication.
                    Impactful
                        Being able to properly understand others is extremely important for finding the truth.
                            It's extremely important for [cooperative reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=tIkQysDqkCY4YvrwV_mIfQ_d), and cooperative reasoning is [extremely important](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=ToKUH9kZobFdEN-AU6WWmC3G) for finding the truth.
                            <Costs of misunderstandings>
                                [Critical piggybacking](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=2J5emCtKut8DRA6avr2C4r87)
                                Move to costs of misunderstandings
                        Important for [systematic reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=XUvhNLQybh6UlJJgJCSnbDU7).
                    Difficult
                        Not properly understanding even one of the key sections here can make it practically impossible to change your mind when it's reasonable to in many scenarios. So a lot of learning is required to properly follow this section.
                            __Not properly understanding even a couple of the key sections here can__ multiply the [time required to resolve disagreements] by a very large number.

                            Relevance
                Semantics
                Reorganize. Especially definitions, conflations and being clear.
                    Definition
                        Semantics is the study of words, sentences and phrases and the meaning that is drawn from them in different contexts.
                    Importance
                        Common
                            Semantics underlie virtually all communication whatsoever, even a lot of internal communication with yourself.
                        Impactful
                            Good reasoning often requires good semantics.
                                [Conflations](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=rkFEurnAxeGlEmMJ8RQUkGO2)
                                    It's very hard to consistently avoid conflations without understanding semantics deeper than average.
                                    Relevance
                                        [How conflations arise](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=mDA22AS-AvwyVGg9b3bT9m8y)
                                <Link to the costs of misunderstandings>
                    Vague wording
                        Definition
                            The topic of vague wording. How to recognize it, what to do about it, etc.
                            **Especially:**   Vague definitions/meanings.
                        Importance
                            Common
                            Very bad for reasoning
                                Vague definitions frequently cause [conflations](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=rkFEurnAxeGlEmMJ8RQUkGO2).
                                Likelihood & Relevance
                                    Conflations are [very bad](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=FbaBK4fH-iKO0a1B7o5S5QFf) for reasoning.
                                    Relevance
                                Vague definitions typically cause a lot of [definitional differences](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=vMjtaIQiRY359z8Zq6mtQRGc)
                                Likelihood & Relevance
                        "Or similar" definitions
                            Definition
                                Definitions in which (a) major component(s) are paired with a qualifier such as "such as", "or similar", "or something like that", etc. without adequate clarification on which concepts would be regarded as "similar"/etc.
                                    "Adequate clarification" meaning sufficient clarification that it can be reasonably expected (from the perspective of the definition-giver, with >75% confidence) that the definition-receiver will adequately understand which concepts would be regarded as "similar"/etc.
                                        "Adequately understand" meaning understand well enough to avoid significant misunderstanding(s).
                        Recognizing vague wording
                        Dealing with vague wording
                            Asking what they mean
                            Accounting for definitional possibilities
                            This might be repeat section. Check and link and resolve if so.
                                Importance
                                ^ Impactful
                                ^ Good reading comprehension by accounting for different possibilities when other people use vague wording.
                        Avoiding vague wording
                            Use the longer clearly-spelled-out version
                                Importance / Limitations
                                ^ Impactful
                                ^ Not always practical.
                                    Spelled-out version is sometimes much longer.
                                    The same idea is sometimes used many times.
                        Examples
                            That, this, it, them, those, etc.
                            Example [free speech](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=8bbYQqmSaf6jvExF2SzbW9vU) definition misunderstanding
                                Two statements using different definitions:
                                ^ "Free speech is sacred" meaning "Government censorship should be minimal".
                                ^ "Free speech has limits" meaning "Private platforms can moderate content".
                                Here it appears that either "free speech" or "sacred/limits" is being defined differently between the two parties, likely causing them to talk past each other.
                        Related
                            [Definitions](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=trb9nqsaLcvBK2O1-HBNApOW)
                            [Definition via analogy](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=wqjHe0ETccAnBhGoYUCfWKtS)
                    Definitions
                        Importance
                            Impactful
                                So incredibly often, disagreements and misunderstandings arise simply because of people using subtly different definitions and bring unable to resolve it (at least in a timely manner).
                        Specific definitions
                            Note
                                Unless otherwise stated, each definition also applies (although usually with slight modifications) to very similar words.
                                    Example
                                        The definitions for "know" apply (except for the obvious change about how the word would be used) to "known".
                            Importance
                            Formal and informal
                                Reasoning
                                    [Informal reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=o4Kl-VNmNYvxA36KNy3kmjie)
                                    Formal reasoning
                                    Move, probably to informal reasoning. Make sure that backlinks are preserved in the process.
                                        Definition
                                            The process of drawing valid inferences in a well-structured and irrefutable (given certain axioms) manner.
                                            Distinctions
                                                This is not to suggest that the premises we begin with in this process necessarily need to be irrefutable.
                                                Nor is it to suggest that we cannot make mistakes in determining whether an argument is valid or not while using formal reasoning, just that under normal conditions validity is technically ensured.
                                        Importance
                                            Very important for [systematic reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=XUvhNLQybh6UlJJgJCSnbDU7).
                                                Helps a lot with [precision](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=581SfOCyfIekfCaptWzmdIKD).
                                                Likelihood
                                                    Representing ideas formally tends to require representing them precisely, without ambiguity.
                                                    Likelihood
                                                        Formalisms tend to be completely unambiguous.
                                                        It's possible (and common) to represent the informal aspect as eg. a premise in a formal argument.
                                                            By having the knowledge to represent the rest of it in a formal manner, one would likely have a much easier time representing or supporting the informal parts in a more formal manner upon request.
                                                            Relevance
                                                                Therefore the knowledge of formal reasoning could still help a lot with precision.
                                                                Relevance
                                                            Even in this case, much of the reasoning is likely made formal in transforming the processes from the premises to the conclusion into a formal argument.
                                                            Relevance
                                                Helps a lot with [thoroughness](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=lj9jejrk2s5bCXgZLKLHwWkZ).
                                                Likelihood
                                                    If one skips over an important step of the formal process, it tends be obvious and able to be pointed out easily.
                                                    Likelihood
                                                        Therefore it would often help a lot with being thorough, by making it easy to see where one is not thorough and where one must be more thorough to completely represent their position formally.
                                                        Relevance
                                                [Importance of systematic reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=XUvhNLQybh6UlJJgJCSnbDU7)
                                                Relevance
                                    Related
                                        [Epistemic rationality](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=rZcLNKNmVyYYwMjNA5z_NhQs)
                                Debate
                                    Formal debates often involve specific preparation, timers and rounds, a moderator, etc.
                                    Informal debate is typically spontaneous, unmoderated, untimed and unstructured.
                                Colloquial
                                    This typically has to do with something like social atmosphere.
                                Argument
                                    A process of reasoning consisting of one or more premises (statements providing evidence or support) that lead to a conclusion (the claim being proven).
                                    In formal contexts, "argument" is usually used to specify a structured version of the above, where the premises, conclusion and inferences are all explicitly represented as such.
                                Rationality
                                    Epistemic rationality
                                        The practice of systematically aligning your beliefs with the truth and updating your worldview based on objective evidence.
                                        Distinction
                                            [Instrumental rationality](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=7F1Qi_G5J8CUa-W8lMXPlNHs)
                                                Epistemic rationality is often quite useful for instrumental rationality, but some specific aspects of epistemic rationality don't improve instrumental rationality much.
                                                    Eg. In some cases one knows what would be the best way to act to achieve their goals, but they don't actually do it.
                                                        Eg. One might know that the best way to convince another person is by speaking calmly with them, but then still end up shouting at them.
                                                Sometimes it even reduces it.
                                                    Eg. Deluding yourself into thinking that you're more attractive than you are might make you feel more confident, which might make you more effective at achieving your goals.
                                                    However this is likely quite rare.
                                                        Long-term, there are typically other strategies for achieving emotional effects like confidence, without the potentially huge cost of getting into the habit of deluding yourself in an emotionally pleasant manner.
                                                        ^ The habit of emotionally deluding one's self in a pleasant manner tends to frequently cause of a ton of [cognitive biases](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=a4amRVifCY8jNCgNpW6j6zB9).
                                                            [Wishful thinking](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=GSuqwuWjSYY3yCdYSuAEztWz)
                                                            [Confirmation bias](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=_Dn0UzSi_JF-Rno7Uvb0luL-)
                                                            [Groupthink](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=1krHbDONylAxWz1bingFgOlj)
                                                            [Rationalization](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=NaE-8bpB1ZDuRzcl_T3nNErK)
                                                            [Sunk cost fallacy](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=MLF635GdLKFJg35pZZA-ER2r)
                                                            [Gambler's fallacy](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=Z811xW5hpftJOBiJ4nLo12ez)
                                    Instrumental rationality
                                        Acting in accordance with your fundamental goals, whatever those are.
                                        Distinction
                                            "your [...] goals" as in the goals that you hold, not necessarily selfish/self-interested goals.
                                    Emotionless rationality
                                        Lacking emotion or passion.
                                        Distinction
                                            [Epistemic rationality](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=rZcLNKNmVyYYwMjNA5z_NhQs)
                                                Trying to repress one's emotions tends to lead to lots of issues that get in the way of [epistemic rationality](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=rZcLNKNmVyYYwMjNA5z_NhQs), and it tends to be correlated with a conflation of epistemic rationality with emotionless rationality, which would of course be correlated with a lack of epistemic rationality.
                                                Link to section about repression
                                    Source
                                        [What is rationality? Short video](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iloTS0wU9qM)
                            Logic
                                0 order (prop)
                                    [True and false (standard)](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=J0b6o4lhMZ0f_F8xHttCI-ng)
                                    Inverse
                                        Adds a "NOT" to both sides of a syllogism.
                                        Check if it actually is a syllogism, link whatever it really is, and link NOT.
                                        Example
                                            The inverse of P→Q is ¬P→¬Q.
                                        Notes
                                            The inverse of a statement is logically equivalent to the [converse](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=hn5cIVc2DKo-2jmUg5S_fwSh) of that statement.
                                        [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inverse_(logic))
                                    Converse
                                        [Parent definition](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=Wac9sjLWcR3Fq8BN9O3Kqvb6)
                                        The result of reversing the two variables.
                                        Maybe change the term "variables" to wherever the standard term is in prop log.
                                        Example
                                            For the implication P → Q, the converse is Q → P.
                                        [Nuance](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=AP6i_jhyeBECDrnuYTZKz1OE)
                                        [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Converse_(logic))
                                    Contrapositive
                                        The inference of going from a conditional statement into its logically equivalent contrapositive.
                                        The contrapositive of a statement has its antecedent and consequent negated and swapped.
                                            The contrapositive of P→Q is ¬Q→¬P.
                                                If P, Then Q. — If not Q, Then not P.
                                        Example
                                            "If it is raining, then I wear my coat." — "If I don't wear my coat, then it isn't raining."
                                        The law of contraposition
                                            The law of contraposition says that a conditional statement is true if, and only if, its contrapositive is true.
                                            [Proof by contrapositive](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=tTENdpA_M33m5Fl4CRqQiy98)
                                        Synonym
                                            Transposition
                                        https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contraposition
                                    Well-defined proposition
                                    Reconcile with [well-defined propositions](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=ewojo1Kk7SCQ_tTLnAMkJeio)
                                        Definition
                                            A proposition whose definition is assigns it a single correct truth value.
                                            Synonym:   [Well-formed formula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Well-formed_formula)
                                            Related
                                                [Well-defined expression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Well-defined_expression)
                                    Inference rule
                                        **Definition:**   A logical pattern that allows one to deduce a valid conclusion from a set of given premise(s).
                                1 order (pred)
                                    Proper part
                                        A part of something that is not the whole of that thing.
                                    Converse
                                        The result of reversing its two constituent statements.
                                        Examples
                                            [Prop example](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=TXNXLJutVGKGljMNwLlbjzPX)
                                            For the categorical proposition "All S are P", the converse is "All P are S".
                                        Nuance
                                            The truth of the converse is generally independent from that of the original statement.
                                        [Wikipedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Converse_(logic))
                            Probabilities
                                Probability
                                    Importance
                                        **Difficulty:**   It's very easy to conflate many of these definitions of probability.
                                            This can result in making bad decisions based on conflating the definitions.
                                            Relevance
                                    Plausibility
                                        A quantification of how plausible an event or proposition is, given our state of knowledge/ignorance.
                                        Example
                                            Fair coin toss
                                                Given the plausibility definition, the coin toss has a 50% probability of landing on each side because we don't have any reason to pick one over the other. i.e. The [principle of indifference](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=nwdnsuvq_ylA7Zc7YVfSoowC) combined with the knowledge that there are two possible outcomes.
                                                Distinction
                                                    We're talking about an idealized scenario where you have absolutely no evidence for the coin tending to land on one side or the other.
                                                    In reality, [coins are slightly more likely to land on the side that starts facing up](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=9VwOn5x7VAs).
                                        Related
                                            Plausibility school of thought
                                            Maybe create a section for this?
                                                This definitions falls under the plausibility school of thought.
                                            [Bayesian inference](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=wnbqSpA8PlB1hhUg-ZjkDFj9)
                                                It's the definition typically used in bayesian reasoning.
                                                    Although it's possible to use bayesian reasoning with [propensity](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=FSrVYvon6XRX2Q4b71AMcYhc) as well.
                                    Credence
                                        The subjective probability we assign to things based (in part) on the evidence available to us as individuals.
                                        Example
                                            Dice
                                                Typically has an equal subjective probability (or credence) of landing on any particular side.
                                                While the physics likely objectively at-least-virtually determine the result once the dice is thrown, given our human limitations, we do not typically have the means to predict the result with more-than-extremely-slightly-better-than-random accuracy.
                                        Synonyms
                                            Confidence
                                                Confidence in a proposition/event X.
                                                Distinctions
                                                    Different from one's "confidence" in propositions/events __in general__ like in [epistemic self-confidence](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=Y9tqRoYVuJ-Fx4nqtdo3klx9).
                                                    Different from one's "confidence", as in [self-esteem](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=5mmCXq5NdWjuCdTW4wQgRgGE).
                                                    Different from one's "confidence", as in how confident they appear, such as during some kind of [persuasion](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=S-S1oq4cZbPSPeH4eYJKd9K7).
                                            Subjective probability
                                            Epistemic probability
                                    Frequentist probability
                                        Defined in terms of the limit of the frequency of an event occurring.
                                        Example
                                            Fair coin toss
                                                Given the frequentist definition, the coin would have a 50% probability of landing on each side because if we would keep flipping it, the ratio of the two outcomes would approach 1/1, so the fraction of either one happening takes up half the total possibility space.
                                                [Distinction](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=N78C3EULjx6kCZjoayqK6AlG)
                                    Propensity
                                    Consider combining this with [frequentist probability](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=vdQH8d59lQKL0q68J2ZjZvH_). I'm unsure about it because the definition of "frequentist probability" I came across (in 3swap video) would seem to consider a coinflip in terms of repeated __very similar__ events, whereas the definition I have here seems to only be about events/propositions that are __exactly the same__. Should probably look into it deeper at some point.
                                        The actual, real probability of events occurring / propositions being true.
                                        Examples
                                            Dice
                                                Typically has a ~100% propensity to land on the side it lands on, at least once it's thrown. Because:
                                                    ("At least once it's thrown", because we don't intend to make claims against free will in this example.)
                                                Dice are typically atleast nearly entirely determined by the laws of physics while falling through the air, in such a way that the final result is typically at least virtually guaranteed, given the exact same starting conditions.
                                            Determinism
                                                If determinism is true, everything is entirely determined to occur from previous events and there is no randomness, so each event objectively either has 0% or 100% propensity to occur.
                                            Quantum mechanics
                                                Might involve interactions that follow genuinely random probability distributions, so the propensity of different quantum events may be quite varied.
                                        Synonyms
                                            Objective probability
                                            Chance
                            Informal
                                [True and false (standard)](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=J0b6o4lhMZ0f_F8xHttCI-ng)
                                True and false (probability)
                                    True: Usually high-probability beliefs, occasionally axioms.
                                    False: Low-probability beliefs.
                                    These definitions are uncommon.
                                        Typically the uncertainty in statements like "I know it's true that we have bread." lies in the word "know" rather than the word "true".
                                            [Know (probability)](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=TnFde8i_liH0vcSg8sIc-HEA)
                                "Soft" reasoning
                                    Definition
                                        Reasoning that cannot easily be broken down to a formal process using any typical methods, and that thus requires an unorthodox and/or informal process.
                                    Importance
                                        Impactful
                                            "Soft" reasoning makes up a large portion of important reasoning.
                                Hot/cold biases
                                Improve
                                    Hot biases
                                    Link a bunch of biases here to categorize them, and maybe add this to related under cognitive biases.
                                        Motivated irrationality where our interests, emotional responses or visceral reactions to things influences our thinking process.
                                        Related: [Cognitive biases](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=a4amRVifCY8jNCgNpW6j6zB9)
                                    Cold biases
                                    Link a bunch of biases here to categorize them, and maybe add this to related under cognitive biases.
                                        Unmotivated irrationality which are a result of certain mental shortcuts and routines we rely on even in situations where they do not really apply.
                                        Related: [Cognitive biases](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=a4amRVifCY8jNCgNpW6j6zB9)
                                Free speech
                                    
                                    "Free speech" is a vague term that should ideally be defined very explicitly before engaging in a serious discussion that uses it.
                                        [Example misunderstanding](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=DRI9Yp8qNoAXyRwU-LhqBfAr)
                                Ad hoc
                                    Science and philosophy definition
                                        The addition of extraneous [hypotheses](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=lelHmq5_RA_nj89mdbd500nr) to save another hypothesis from being falsified.
                                        Link to falsification
                                        Ad hoc hypotheses compensate for anomalies not anticipated by the theory in its unmodified form.
                                    [Source](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ad_hoc)
                                Informal operations
                                    OR
                                        Depending on the context, it can mean https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=n7OMAZ2eLgm2YIZTBh-L2db8 or [standard OR](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=TKmTc0y15-zDJqP-9eeA6L5Z).
                                    IF-THEN
                                        Definition
                                            Usually a [material conditional](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=uzxNZgNX8Jlzb09GO2ZXwiQw) with the added requirement that there be some causal or epistemic relation between the condition and consequence.
                                            Sometimes instead a [IF-AND-ONLY-IF (material biconditional)](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=EllGLMOpw-VRb31hYJiNtBhw).
                                                Example: "I'll buy you a new wallet if you need one" may be interpreted as a [biconditional](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=EllGLMOpw-VRb31hYJiNtBhw) ("if and only if"), since the speaker doesn't intend a valid outcome to be buying the wallet whether or not the wallet is needed (as in a [conditional](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=uzxNZgNX8Jlzb09GO2ZXwiQw)).
                            Misc
                                Know
                                    Know (certainty)
                                    Know (probability)
                                        Know: Have more than C credence in something being true.
                                        Typically C is more than 85% and less than 100%.
                                        Distinction
                                            Distinct from [know (certainty)](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=ytpWye4oZ5q5dogPtKSCz111)
                                                Less than 100%.
                                Good/bad/etc.
                                    Moral/axiological
                                    For reasoning
                                        Good for reasoning, bad for reasoning, etc.
                                        This definition is uncommon, but for this particular context (a reasoning guide) we use it for convenience.
                                Philosophical logic
                                    The mathematical investigation of basic notions of logic.
                                    The deployment of logic to help with mathematical problems, so ‘philosophical logic’ means both (a) the philosophical investigation of the basic notions of logic and (b) the deployment of logic to help with philosophical problems.
                                    In the context of this guide, in largely includes these sections:
                                        [Axioms](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=HTSBFQMP49xI2F7tHDD5P1pd)
                                        [Standard deduction](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=ENg9uidRSS0t3eQBEFX4pGmm)
                                        [Probabilistic reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=i_iQ7vvMYVnf1xdY5Ymr8--m)
                                        [Expression/interpretation](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=K_SHB0cGTZkUKMGU-ep5cX4R)
                            Unusual but used here
                                Definition
                                    Definitions that are unusual for the term they are defining, but used in this reasoning guide.
                                [Dynalist "items"](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=ysqXDunJUGkagJZq3yN87Atd)

                                General Reasoning Guide
                                    **Definition:**   The title of this guide.
                                    [General Reasoning Guide        Pre-Alpha v0.1.7.4](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd)
                                    Related
                                        [FAQs](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=zKXsMJmmMm-VEFAVMo0P4xWB) - For more misc info about this guide.
                                Made-up terms
                                    Definition
                                        Some relevant terms that we've made up, to make it easier to talk about certain concepts.
                                        Note that this probably doesn't include all the made-up terms used throughout the guide, but hopefully most of them.
                                    Importance / Limitations
                                        Probably not very useful since nobody uses these terms.
                                        Could maybe be nice for communities wanting to adopt some misc handy short-cut terms.
                                    [Critical piggybacking](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=2J5emCtKut8DRA6avr2C4r87)
                                    [Other-shoe reviews](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=d7AlWLW-6EAuja2PutdZEj64)
                                    RAC
                                        Definition
                                            RAC is an acronym for "rationally action-compelling", which means:
                                            Truly better to have/do (all else being equal) in a sense that is action-compelling to a perfectly rational agent, without needing any moral/axiological axioms/presuppositions.
                                            i.e. / expounding
                                                In other words, a proposed kind of ought that can be derived epistemically from non-oughts, and which would, if its potential existence is known by a perfectly rational agent, compel that perfectly rational agent to "act in accordance with" it, for rational reasons."
                                                "Act in accordance with" being defined as "attempt to (in the absence of sufficient competing RAC or potentially RAC things) maximize the average* (or mean, etc.) completion of". "Action-compelling" being defined similarly.
                                                `*` "Average completion" or alternatives typically being defined in terms of subjective probability, rather than objective probability. However this might change depending on the context.
                                    Literaloo
                                        **Definition:**   Literally literally
                                        Importance
                                            There are a decent number of situations where you want to clarify that you mean something literally, but there isn't an easy way to do so because the normal explicit methods have other connotations.
                                                For example it might be interpreted as rude, and prefacing what you say with "literally" is likely just going to sound like emphasis of the rude thing.
                        Definitional options
                            Recommended options
                                Most common definition
                                    Definition
                                        The current most common definition in the world.
                                    Should be the default choice in most situations.
                                Most common definition (given broad context)
                                    Definition
                                        The current most common definition given the broad context. 
                                            Broad context
                                        Examples
                                Other's definition
                                    Definition
                                        The definition that the person(s) you're having the discussion with appear(s) to be using.
                                    Limitations
                                        Difficulty of guessing definitions
                                        Potential conflations
                                            The other person may be conflating multiple definitions, meaning using their definition may cause more confusion.
                                Making one up
                                    Limitations
                                        If there is an already-present definition, it can cause a lot of confusion to make one up instead.
                                    How to view it
                                        If no definition fitting one of the other options works well, writing your own may be the most efficient option despite the potential confusion.
                                How to choose
                            Unrecommended options
                                [Vague definitions](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=0gOG4jQ-x49IDTjJn9kHifS6)
                                    Why to avoid
                                        To avoid [conflating ideas](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=rkFEurnAxeGlEmMJ8RQUkGO2)
                                            [Vague definitions frequently cause conflations.](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=wsPeD0rbc6QiT5c6ud5AwvkB)
                                        To avoid confusing them
                                Etymology-based definition
                                    Definition
                                        Definition based primarily on the etymology of the word.
                                    Why to avoid
                                        Confusion
                                        Reasons to adopt
                                            "Deeper truths"
                                                Definition
                                                    The view that the etymology of words hide deeper truths about those words.
                                                    This is a semi-common view, particularly among conspiracy theorists.
                                How to avoid
                        Definitional consistency
                            Definition
                            Importance
                                Changing a definition mid-discussion often causes insane amounts of confusion (usually for both parties).
                                    Exceptions
                                        If you make it very clear when you're using a different definition and what that other definition is, most confusion can usually be avoided.
                                Unknowingly using multiple definitions is called "conflation" and is one of the biggest causes for faulty reasoning ever.
                            Methods
                                Pick a definition and stick with it
                                    This is the most reliable way to avoid conflations and semantic confusion.
                        Definitional differences
                            Importance
                                When you and the other person are using different definitions, it's very important to recognize and fix this, otherwise you could end up talking past each other for a long time.
                            Types of definitional differences
                                Different definitions
                                    Definition
                                        This is the typical case where people have different definitions for the same word.
                                    Examples
                                        The hot dog ran
                                            The dog (animal) that was hot (temperature) ran.
                                            The dog (animal) that was hot (attractive) ran.
                                            The "hot dog" (food) ran.
                                Different sub-definitions
                                    Definition
                                        Sub-definition
                                        ^ A definition for a (word that is inside of a definition for the main word in question).
                                        Example
                                            Two people may appear to be using the same standard definition for a classical God, but define one of the relevant properties (eg. omnipotence) differently. One might define it as maximally powerful (as powerful as possible within logical constraints), while another may define it as having power over absolutely everything, including logic.
                                            ^ The definition for classical theism just mentions "omnipotence", so they can both point to the same definition and think they're talking about the same concept, but due to the different definition of the term *inside* the definition for classical theism, they are actually talking about different concepts.
                                    Importance
                                        Impactful
                                        ^ People can seem to agree on the main definition due to using the same words, but they can actually mean separate things due to defining part(s) of the definition for the main word differently.
                                            This can lead to a significant amount of time wasted from misunderstandings, perhaps making the difference between changing someone's mind / understanding someone, and not.
                                            [Example](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=p6U8FY4qOsccNJ3l8cqZaaD2)
                                            Likelihood
                                Different "orders of operations"
                                    Definition
                                        Abiguity due to not knowing which parts to read as connected to which other parts.
                                    Examples
                                        A definition for a word that is inside of a definition for the main word in question.
                                            A definition for a (word that is inside of a definition for the main word in question).
                                            (A definition for a word) that is inside of a definition for the main word in question.
                                Assumed details
                                    People sometimes assume details for a term that weren't explicitly given.
                                    These assumed details can often differ from the intended details, if there were even intended details in the first place.
                            Recognizing when definitional differences occur
                                Importance
                                    Impactful
                                    ^ When people say things that seem very obviously wrong, it is very often due to some definitional difference.
                                Checking for possible interpretations
                                Reorganize or split this into other sections here? Not sure
                                    Definition
                                        Checking for different ways that a person could be using terminology.
