                (Un)conservative claims
                    Definition
                        Claims and how broad and/or confident they are.
                    Importance
                        Impactful
                            It's important to form good habits about what kind of claims to make, to be more [open minded](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=z7LAOrlY0wVUk3aV25kvfWZe)
                            Useful for [persuasion](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=S-S1oq4cZbPSPeH4eYJKd9K7)
                            ~~Expert
                    Unconservative claims
                        Confident claims
                            Importance
                                Typically very important to avoid due to [limitations](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=xsu2gMpUxsR6ewr50RhWVW_9)
                                Can be useful for [persuasion](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=S-S1oq4cZbPSPeH4eYJKd9K7)
                                ~~Adept, support
                            Limitations
                                Even if we are justified in having more confident beliefs about more major claims, doing so is often not ideal because it "closes the doors behind us". If we're pushed back with evidence, we emotionally have nowhere to go and are often prone to get defensive and more likely to refuse the truth. ([Source](https://youtu.be/CkJc6c3nKMw))
                                    Video chosen because it's the best quick and straightforward demonstration I'm aware of, not because of the atheist angle the video creator chooses to take with it.
                        Major claims
                            Definition
                                Claims which are very broad.
                                Example
                                    All squares have four 90° angles.
                                    All Nazis were 100% evil.
                                    2 + 2 always equals 4.
                            Importance
                                It's very important to be able to discriminate from justified major claims and unjustified major claims, as the can often appear far more or less justified than they really are.
                                ^ Typically because of failing to adequately account for the [prior probability](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=WtCnPwTlo9i-Whi4OhvH_ZQd)
                            Limitations
                                Often mistaken
                                    It's rare that practical things are entirely black and white / all or nothing, usually (unless dealing with purely abstract concepts or something) there is some nuance/exception.
                                Encourages defensiveness
                                    Major claims are often made (or seem to be made) confidently.
                                        [Confident claims](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=R5pa44kr5Rew69QsnuVi9P00)
                                        ^ Made more damaging by the fact that major claims are [often mistaken](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=dIqzMY64S7pUDKKhP5VdhBRD)
                            How to view
                                Aside from statements like [this](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=mlhLMUmKfAicTAN3-3-egkYg) where you have a solid deductive proof to back the broad claims up, or in situations where the evidence is quite overwhelming, it is usually best to avoid making such major claims.
                                And even in the exceptional cases where you're likely right, it is typically best to speak less confidently than you feel, so as to make the process of changing your mind more comfortable if the situation happens to call for it.
                            Justified major claims
                                Deductive [proofs](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=FkzQqkwmEP9ECLN3x7wo6x_O)
                                Overwhelming evidence
                                    Overwhelming evidence for the generalization being very reliable
                    Related
                        [Distinguishing likelihood and relevance](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=yhNvheql8sUOE-_HhGsNwMvd)
                Argument premoves
                    Definition
                        Attempting to account for possible counterarguments before they are given.
                    Importance / limitations
                        Common
                            At least small examples of this are very common.
                        Impactful
                            It often feels like addressing relevant position(s) when it actually isn't.
                                [Limitations of addressing irrelevant reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=GpDBQ5VtNgWsY6aQCQ8MESNG)
                            Can save time
                                You really have to know what you're doing to consistently save time.
                                It can also waste a lot of time from [issues resulting from addressing irrelevant reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=GpDBQ5VtNgWsY6aQCQ8MESNG)
                    Recommended alternative
                        It's usually better to ask what one believes and mostly only respond to what you can be very confident is their position.
                        ^ [Limitations of addressing irrelevant reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=GpDBQ5VtNgWsY6aQCQ8MESNG)
                    Related
                        [Addressing irrelevant reasoning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=KOPPXTY3kepYJVMbJ9RL4sXR)
                            A very common downside of argument premoves.
                        [Steelmanning](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=LWB8YQUQupE7UQRtFL7J9g6w)
                            Argument premoves are a very common technique used when attempting to steelman others.
                Inflammatory statements
                    Definition
                        Provocative or emotionally charged remarks.
                        **Often:**   Intended to provoke strong reactions (typically negative), often anger or outrage.
                    Importance / Limitations
                        Common
                        Impactful
                            Using inflammatory statements often causes people to launch inflammatory statements back, intended to make you feel a similarly negative way.
                                If these attempts are even remotely successful, it's typically an epistemic problem because it could easily cause you to misunderstand and/or unintentionally strawman their position.
                                Link how mood (especially anger) effects our reasoning.
                                    We often believe that it wouldn't influence us when it actually would.
                                    Try to find the study on how people cared about what other people thought of them even when they expected otherwise.
                                This can lead you to further dehumanize them and take what they say even less seriously, often less than make sense.
                Informal arguments
                    Definition
                        Arguments which are given in ordinary language.
                    Importance
                        Common
                            Most arguments are informal, as opposed to [formal](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=0At0cZGMuQERz1v4oedfKRza).
                        Difficult
                            In an informal argument, it is often difficult to see what the premises and the conclusion are.
                                 Informal arguments often contains material which is inessential to the argument.
                                    Much of what people say or write has a rhetorical purpose.
                    Related
                        As opposed to [standard form arguments](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=WBGbs-oyLu2VHlBm5Vkh-KAb)
                Related
                    [Conflations](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=rkFEurnAxeGlEmMJ8RQUkGO2)
                    [Fitting things together](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=FORaGWzKq7OJtxVu6LDAqa11)
                        Mentally fitting concepts together in a logical way is crucial for being able to explain your position to people who are not accustomed to your mental map of concepts.
                            You may need to explain it in completely different terms and in relation to completely different concepts than you're accustomed to.
                            ^ Being able to follow connections to those alternative areas is very important for this.
                    [Examples](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=rWwkVHO702PBy1aoUtBw-bBU)
                    [Analogies](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=fB49ZDXwTg85jeD3n0Jft40n)
                    [Heavily relying on implied premises](https://dynalist.io/d/nBfl0bh1yEuK5cktkexuu8Xd#z=qmBqfPbnbOqR5hgHr1RnIegw)
